# BlackOut Trades ‚Äî Audit Findings (living doc)

Verified issues from the production data-correctness audit. Newest/most-severe first.
Cross-provider ground truth: Polygon + Unusual Whales REST. Started 2026-07-01.

**Merge policy for this doc's PRs:** left OPEN for end-of-day review ‚Äî do not merge without explicit go-ahead, even when CI is green. **Superseded 2026-07-03 by explicit user standing instruction to run fully autonomously (branch‚Üífix‚Üítest‚ÜíPR‚ÜíCI‚Üímerge‚Üílive-verify, repeat) through Monday 2026-07-06 market open ‚Äî this doc's entries merge immediately alongside their fix PRs for the remainder of that window.**

**Process note, 2026-07-04:** working through the full CEO/CTO audit's remaining ~21 findings back-to-back per explicit "fix everything, don't stop" instruction. Per-fix local verification (tsc/test/build/lint/auth-guards) and a FINDINGS.md entry stay mandatory for every fix; the separate docs-only "deploy confirmed SUCCESS" follow-up PR used earlier tonight is dropped for this batch to avoid serializing ~20 fixes behind ~20 extra PRs ‚Äî Railway deploy health is spot-checked periodically instead of after every single merge. **Scope note:** the earlier standing "UI is Cursor's job" boundary was specifically about the landing-page BIE banner design work; this "fix everything from the audit" instruction is broader and explicit, so a few of the remaining findings do touch `.tsx` files (`FlowAlertStream.tsx`, `NetPremiumLeaderboard.tsx`, `ZeroDteBoard.tsx`) ‚Äî each one is a surgical logic-only bug fix (a DTE calculation, a loading-state prop, a freshness signal), never a visual/layout change, to stay out of the way of Cursor's active design work on the same components. **Tooling note:** the GitHub MCP proxy's session quota is separately rate-limited from the underlying GitHub API (confirmed: REST via a direct token has ~14.8k/15k requests remaining while the MCP proxy returned "rate limit exceeded") ‚Äî from here on, PRs are opened directly ready-for-review (skipping the draft‚Üíready round trip) and comment/review checks use direct REST calls, to conserve that budget for the unavoidable create/merge calls.

**Follow-up sweep, 2026-07-04 (post-launch):** all 23 original CEO/CTO audit items closed and merged to `main` (PRs #435/#437/#439/#441/#442); `PG_POOL_MAX=4` also applied directly to the Railway `blackout-web` production service and a redeploy triggered to pick it up (both with explicit user confirmation ‚Äî see the PG_POOL_MAX entry below for why this couldn't be done from a PR alone). A second, independent audit pass was then run against the resulting `main` specifically hunting for anything the first pass's blast-radius checks missed (same fail-open/duplication/rounding/grounding bug classes, new files). It found 9 more issues, all now closed ‚Äî this was the 9th and last.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `fetchEcosystemContext()` never read SPX Slayer's own tables ‚Äî the play engine was invisible to itself (BIE/Largo integration sweep, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts::fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` is BIE's per-ticker cross-instrument snapshot ‚Äî the single query layer that the admin BIE report, Largo's `get_ecosystem_context` tool, and precedent-search ingestion all flow through to answer "what does the rest of the platform know about this ticker." Its `EcosystemContext` type (lines 76-94 pre-fix) read `zerodte_setup_log` (`zerodte_today`), `nighthawk_play_outcomes` (`nighthawk_recent`), `alert_audit_log` (`recent_audit_entries`), and `flow_alerts`/`flow_anomalies` (`recent_flow`/`recent_anomalies`) ‚Äî every cross-instrument write path EXCEPT SPX Slayer's own `spx_open_play`/`spx_play_outcomes`/`spx_signal_log`. Confirmed by grep: zero references to any `spx_*` table anywhere in `ecosystem-context.ts` before this fix. So a member or Largo asking this function "what's going on with SPX" got 0DTE + Night Hawk + flow, but never SPX Slayer's own live/recent play state ‚Äî the one instrument this sweep is strengthening BIE/Largo integration for.

**Fix:** added `spx_play: EcosystemSpxPlay | null` to `EcosystemContext`, shaped `{ open_play: {...} | null, last_closed: {...} | null }` ‚Äî deliberately a single most-recent open + single most-recent closed play, matching `nighthawk_recent`'s "one current take, not a history array" precedent rather than `recent_audit_entries`'s list shape. Populated ONLY when `ticker` is `"SPX"` or `"SPXW"`; `null` for every other ticker. Sourced via the exact fetchers `src/lib/platform/spx-service.ts` already calls for the same tables (`getSpxOpenPlay` ‚Üí `fetchOpenSpxPlay(todayEtYmd())`; `getSpxTradeHistory` ‚Üí `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes(limit)`, here called with `limit=1` since only the most recent closed play is needed) ‚Äî no new SQL, no new write path, both imported straight from `src/lib/db.ts`.

**Ticker-scoping note (why a conditional fetch, not a `WHERE ticker = $1`):** `zerodte_today`/`nighthawk_recent` scope to the requested ticker via a SQL `WHERE` clause because their source tables carry a `ticker` column. `spx_open_play`/`spx_play_outcomes` carry **no ticker column at all** (confirmed against their `CREATE TABLE` in `db.ts`) ‚Äî SPX Slayer is a single-instrument engine, so there's nothing to filter on. `spx_play` is scoped instead by only calling `fetchOpenSpxPlay`/`fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` when `ticker.toUpperCase()` is `SPX`/`SPXW`, so a non-SPX ticker gets `null` without a query ever running (verified in the new test via a call counter).

**Blast radius:** additive-only. `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` (the `Record<keyof EcosystemContext, string>` that machine-generates BIE's own `platform:bie-capabilities` knowledge doc in `knowledge.ts`) required a matching `spx_play` entry ‚Äî a compile-time-enforced mapping, so this was a `tsc` error, not an optional nicety, until added. `src/lib/largo/run-tool.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` case returns `fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` directly with no per-field serialization, so the new field surfaces to Largo automatically with no code change there. `src/lib/largo/tool-defs.ts`'s `get_ecosystem_context` tool description was updated (small, additive) to mention `spx_play` so Largo's own system-prompt-level tool description doesn't undersell what the tool now returns. `src/app/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts` does NOT call `fetchEcosystemContext` at all (checked directly ‚Äî it composes its own independent set of probes), so no change was needed there. No write path, no schema change, no existing field's shape changed.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (confirms the `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS` compile-time contract stayed satisfied). Full suite `1023/1023` passing ‚Äî 4 new/updated tests in `src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.test.ts` using the `mock.module("../db", ...)` pattern from `nighthawk/platform-intel-snapshot.test.ts`: `spx_play.open_play` populates correctly for ticker `SPX` when an open play exists; `spx_play.last_closed` reflects the most recent closed play for ticker `SPXW`; `spx_play` is `null` for a non-SPX ticker (`AAPL`) AND the SPX-only fetchers are proven never called via a call counter; plus the pre-existing `ECOSYSTEM_CONTEXT_FIELDS` coverage test extended with `spx_play`. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## üßÝ BIE calibration gains SPX Slayer awareness SHIPPED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî two self-improving loops, one report (branch `fix/bie-calibration-spx-slayer`)
**Gap:** `src/lib/bie/calibration.ts`'s `runBieCalibration()` ‚Äî BIE's Layer-5 gate-calibration harness ‚Äî read ONLY `zerodte_setup_log` (0DTE Command's ledger), bucketed by score band / time-of-day / spike, and produced evidence-gated (n‚â•10) recommendations. It had zero awareness that SPX Slayer runs its OWN separate, already-live adaptive-gate calibration loop: `src/lib/spx-play-telemetry.ts`'s `loadAdaptivePlayGates()` reads `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` (`src/lib/spx-play-outcomes.ts`, backed by `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` over `spx_play_outcomes`) and feeds real `global_min_score_boost`/`promote_min_score_boost` adjustments into `spx-play-engine.ts`. Two self-improving loops on the same platform had never been introduced to each other ‚Äî BIE's own calibration report was blind to a whole product's outcome data, even though the fetcher it needed already existed.

**Fix ‚Äî read-only analytics addition, does NOT touch the live engine:** `calibration.ts` now runs a second, parallel bucketing pass over `spx_play_outcomes` (via the SAME `fetchClosedPlayOutcomes` fetcher `spx-play-telemetry.ts` already uses ‚Äî no new SQL) alongside the existing 0DTE pass. New pure functions `computeSpxCalibration`/`formatSpxCalibration` bucket SPX Slayer's own closed plays by **grade band** (`A/A+` / `B` / `C/D`, via the existing `gradeRank` from `spx-play-config.ts` so the band edges can't drift from the live grade-floor gate) and by the **same 4 time-of-day windows** 0DTE already uses (deliberately identical boundaries so the two sections read side by side), applying the identical n‚â•10 evidence gate before emitting any recommendation. Win/loss classification uses the play's own graded `outcome` field (`spx-play-outcomes.ts`'s `classifyOutcome`, which already handles STOP/TARGET/TRAIL/THESIS/THETA/SESSION exit nuance) rather than a raw pnl-sign check, so breakevens are counted as neither a win nor a loss. `CalibrationReport` gains one additive, nullable field ‚Äî `spx_slayer: SpxCalibrationReport | null` ‚Äî set by the new `runBieCalibration()` orchestration step (`computeSpxSlayerCalibration`, isolated in its own try/catch so an SPX-side DB hiccup can never take down the 0DTE half of the report); `computeCalibration()` itself is untouched and always seeds `spx_slayer: null`, so no existing caller's shape or test changes. `formatCalibration()` now labels its own section "0DTE Command calibration" (was bare "BIE calibration") and appends a clearly separated `---`-delimited "SPX Slayer calibration" section when `spx_slayer` is attached ‚Äî both sections keep fully separate bucket sets and recommendation lists, never merged.

**Explicitly NOT touched (blast radius):** `spx-play-telemetry.ts` and `spx-play-engine.ts` ‚Äî SPX Slayer's live adaptive-gate loop (`loadAdaptivePlayGates`, `computeAdaptiveGates`, `effectiveFullMinScore`/`effectivePromoteMinScore`) reads `fetchPlayOutcomeStats()` exactly as before; this PR adds a second, independent read of the same underlying table for reporting only, never feeding anything back into what score-floor/promote adjustments actually apply. `/api/admin/bie-report/route.ts` needed NO code change ‚Äî it already forwards the whole `CalibrationReport` object as `calibration.data` and `formatCalibration(calibration)` as `calibration.text`, so the new field and section flow through automatically; `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` only ever rendered `calibration.text` in a `<pre>` block, so the richer text renders with zero frontend changes.

**Verification:** 5 new tests in `src/lib/bie/bie.test.ts` (nearest existing test file for `calibration.ts` ‚Äî no dedicated `calibration.test.ts` exists; 0DTE's own calibration tests already live there) ‚Äî SPX buckets by grade band and cites evidence; refuses to recommend below n=10 (mirrors the existing 0DTE thin-evidence test); excludes `outcome: "open"` rows from every bucket; combined report shows both "0DTE Command calibration" and "SPX Slayer calibration" headers; without an attached SPX pass the report stays 0DTE-only text (no restructuring). Full suite `1025/1025` passing, `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî SPX Claude play-gate's fabrication guard checked the thesis but not the headline (SPX Slayer/BIE sweep finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`'s `evaluateClaudePlayApproval()` builds a `ClaudePlayVerdict` with both a `headline` (max 12 words) and a `thesis` (2 sentences) ‚Äî the prompt (line ~362) explicitly instructs Claude to put "a specific level or catalyst" in the headline, so it is just as likely to cite a price level as the thesis is. Both fields ship verbatim onto the real-money 0DTE play card the same way. But the post-generation FABRICATION GUARD added by the earlier "SPX Claude play-gate thesis had no fabrication guard" fix (this doc, below) only ever called `checkNumbersGrounded(result.thesis, known)` ‚Äî `result.headline` was never passed to the guard at all. A hallucinated number confined to the headline (e.g. Claude inventing "Breakout toward next major level 6120" when nothing in `knownPlayLevels()` is anywhere near 6120) would sail straight past the guard, get cached, get audit-logged, and ship to paying members ‚Äî while an identical fabrication in the thesis one field over was already being caught. This was found while auditing the SPX Slayer engine's BIE/Largo integration surface for exactly this class of gap (a check applied to one sibling field but not another).

**Why it wasn't caught earlier:** the original fabrication-guard fix (and its test) treated "the thesis" as a stand-in for "Claude's free text," matching the pattern of `gex-heatmap/explain`'s `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded` (which only ever had one narrative string to check). `spx-play-claude.ts` is the only one of the six `checkNumbersGrounded` call sites with two independently-hallucinate-able free-text fields shipping to the same card ‚Äî `spx-commentary.ts` was built (or later fixed) to already join `` `${headline}\n${body}` `` before checking, but `spx-play-claude.ts`'s two-field shape was never cross-checked against that sibling.

**Fix:** `checkNumbersGrounded` now runs against `` `${result.headline} ${result.thesis}` `` (joined, mirroring `spx-commentary.ts`'s existing `headline+body` join) instead of `result.thesis` alone ‚Äî so a fabricated number in either field trips the same guard. On failure, the fallback path is unchanged in shape: discard the whole Claude verdict (not just the offending field) and fall back to `mechanicalVerdict()`, still audit-logged via `logPlayVerdict()`. Renamed the `trigger_reason` string passed to `logPlayVerdict()` from `"ungrounded_claude_thesis"` to `"ungrounded_claude_verdict"` since it can now fire for a headline-only fabrication too and the old name would be actively misleading in the audit trail; confirmed (via repo-wide grep) this string has exactly one producer (`spx-play-claude.ts`) and no consumer pattern-matches its literal value ‚Äî `trigger_reason` is read everywhere else (`AdminBieDashboard.tsx`, `ecosystem-context.ts`, `precedent-search.ts`) as an opaque display/context string, so the rename is safe.

**Blast radius:** scoped to the one grounding check and its log label in `spx-play-claude.ts`. Did not touch the five other `checkNumbersGrounded` call sites (`gex-heatmap/explain`, `flow-brief`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `nights-watch/position-narrative.ts`, `nighthawk/play-critic.ts`, `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`) ‚Äî each already checks its own single narrative string (or, for `spx-commentary.ts`, an already-joined `headline+body`), so none share this two-separately-checked-fields gap.

**Fix rationale:** joining the two fields into one `checkNumbersGrounded` call (rather than two independent calls) was chosen to match the existing `spx-commentary.ts` precedent exactly and because the guard's contract is "does this text cite any number outside the known set" ‚Äî a single joined call and two independent calls are behaviorally equivalent here (either failure is treated identically: discard the whole verdict), so the simpler one-call form was preferred.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. Full suite `1024/1024` passing ‚Äî extended `src/lib/spx-play-claude.test.ts` with: (1) two new unit-level cases proving a headline-only hallucinated level fails the joined `` `${headline} ${thesis}` `` check even though the thesis alone is fully grounded (and passes when both are grounded), directly mirroring the file's existing thesis-only unit tests; (2) two new full-integration cases that actually call `evaluateClaudePlayApproval()` end-to-end with `node:test`'s `mock.module` swapping in a fake `providers/anthropic` (mirroring `nighthawk/play-critic.test.ts`'s pattern for the same bug class) and `DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL` blanked before import (mirroring `nighthawk/discovery-quality.test.ts`, since this sandbox's ambient `DATABASE_URL` points at a Railway-internal host this environment cannot reach) ‚Äî proving a Claude response with a grounded headline+thesis is approved as-is, and one with a fabricated headline number falls back to `source: "mechanical"` with the mechanical (not the fabricated Claude) headline, even though its thesis is independently fully grounded. This closes the gap the original fix's own verification note flagged ("Full async pipeline ‚Äî Claude calls, DB caching ‚Äî not mocked/tested; no existing test harness for that in this file's sibling `spx-play-*.test.ts` files.") ‚Äî `spx-play-claude.test.ts` now has one. `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Live Desk AI grounding-failure discard had no durable audit trail (SPX Slayer/BIE integration sweep, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/providers/spx-commentary.ts`'s `generateSpxCommentary()` runs `checkNumbersGrounded()` against the generated headline+body (the fabrication guard added earlier this session ‚Äî see the "Flagship SPX Live Desk AI commentary had no fabrication guard" entry below) and, on failure, just `return null` (line ~597-602 pre-fix) ‚Äî the caller (`src/app/api/market/spx/commentary/route.ts`) 502s to the client with the rejected text discarded and nothing durable recorded, only an ephemeral `console.warn`. This is the flagship "Live Desk AI" rail on the SPX Slayer dashboard, one shared Claude Haiku call every ~5 minutes cached cluster-wide, so a hallucinated read there is a real, repeatable event worth a trace.

**Contrast that exposed the gap:** the sibling AI-narration surface, `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`'s `logPlayVerdict()` (added the same day this same fabrication-guard work landed on that file), writes a real row to the shared `alert_audit_log` table via `insertAlertAuditLog` on EVERY verdict ‚Äî pass or fail ‚Äî with `alert_type: "spx_claude_play"`. `spx-commentary.ts` got the identical grounding guard in the same audit pass but never got the matching audit-log write, so there was (and until this fix, remained) zero historical trace of how often the dashboard's headline AI rail silently throws away a hallucinated read ‚Äî an observability gap on the platform's single most-viewed AI surface.

**Fix:** added `logUngroundedCommentary(desk, ctx, parsed, grounding)`, called synchronously (never awaited, matching `logPlayVerdict`'s call shape exactly) from the existing `if (!grounding.grounded)` branch, immediately before its unchanged `return null`. It fire-and-forgets a `alert_type: "spx_commentary_ungrounded"` row via `insertAlertAuditLog` (guarded by the same `dbConfigured()` early-return `logPlayVerdict` uses, and a `.catch(err => console.error(...))` so a DB hiccup can never throw into `generateSpxCommentary`'s control flow): `source_table: "spx_commentary"`, `source_key: {price, as_of}`, `ticker: "SPX"`, `direction` set to the model's (untrusted) `bias` so a reviewer can see what stance it was hallucinating in, `confidence_score`/`confidence_label` pulled from the same deterministic `ctx.confluence.score`/`.grade` the prompt itself was built from (never a model self-grade, matching the table's own column-comment contract), `trigger_reason` naming the specific ungrounded value, `decision_trace: [{check: "numbers_grounded", passed: false, value: <the value>}]`, and ‚Äî the part that actually lets someone reconstruct what was rejected ‚Äî `final_output: {headline, body, bias}` holding the raw generated text verbatim (otherwise unrecoverable once discarded) plus an `input_snapshot` of the handful of desk levels (price/vwap/gamma_flip/gex_king/max_pain) the model was looking at, without dumping the whole deeply-nested `ctx` object into every rejected row.

**Blast radius:** purely additive ‚Äî the success path (`return parsed`) and the existing failure path's `console.warn` + `return null` contract to the caller are byte-for-byte unchanged; the caller's 502 behavior on a `null` return is untouched. No other call site references `generateSpxCommentary`'s grounding branch.

**Fix rationale:** mirrored `logPlayVerdict`'s exact shape (module-level `function ...(): void` that internally fire-and-forgets, called synchronously with no `await`/`void` at the call site) rather than inventing a new pattern, since this task is explicitly about closing the asymmetry between the two sibling AI-narration surfaces. Considered logging on the SUCCESS path too (for parity with `logPlayVerdict` logging both outcomes) but deliberately did not ‚Äî the success path already has zero observability gap (the commentary itself gets served and cached, which is its own record), and the standing instruction here scoped this purely to the discard branch.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; new `src/lib/providers/spx-commentary.test.ts` (mocks `./anthropic`, `../grounding-guard`, and `../db` per this repo's `mock.module()` idiom ‚Äî bare specifiers resolve relative to the test file, not the `@/` alias `spx-commentary.ts` itself uses) with 3 cases: a forced-ungrounded generation returns `null` AND fires exactly one `alert_type: "spx_commentary_ungrounded"` audit row with the expected shape; a grounded generation passes through untouched and never touches the audit log; and the write is skipped (while the `null` return stays unchanged) when `dbConfigured()` is false. Full suite passing; `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `portfolioGreeks` aggregation in `/api/account/positions` skipped `roundFloats()` (follow-up audit finding, low ‚Äî last of the 9)
**Where:** `src/app/api/account/positions/route.ts`'s `GET` handler builds `portfolioGreeks` (delta/gamma/theta/vega/totalPremiumAtRisk/totalDeltaDollars) via a `reduce` over open legs' raw valuation greeks, then returned it straight in the JSON response with no rounding ‚Äî unlike the sibling per-position fields in `enrichPosition` (`current_value`, `unrealized_pnl`, `pnl_pct`, etc.), which are all rounded via inline `.toFixed(2)` before being serialized.

**Currently inert, confirmed by tracing the one consumer:** `src/components/nights-watch/NightsWatchPanel.tsx` destructures `data.portfolioGreeks` (line ~1369) but never actually reads it ‚Äî it calls its own local `computePortfolioGreeks(positions)` (defined in the same file) instead, both where the aggregate is displayed and where `liveLegs` is read. So today this bug produces no visible float noise; it's a live landmine for the moment anything (a future UI change, a Largo/BIE tool, an external API consumer) starts reading the field the route already documents itself as providing.

**Fix:** wrapped the field in `roundFloats()` before the response: `portfolioGreeks: roundFloats(portfolioGreeks)`. Left `positions` (the `enriched` array) alone ‚Äî its numeric fields are already rounded via `enrichPosition`'s own inline `.toFixed()` calls, so wrapping the whole response would be redundant.

**Noted but NOT fixed here (out of scope for this fix):** whether `NightsWatchPanel.tsx` should be changed to consume the server-computed `portfolioGreeks` instead of its own client-side `computePortfolioGreeks` recomputation is a design question, not a correctness bug ‚Äî the client computation isn't wrong, just duplicated. Left for a separate decision rather than folded into this fix.

**Blast radius:** one field, one route. No consumer currently reads it, so no behavior change is observable today ‚Äî this fix only prevents a future consumer from inheriting unrounded floats.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1013/1013` passing (no new test ‚Äî `roundFloats()` already has its own direct unit coverage in `round-floats.test.ts`, and this route has no existing test file to extend, matching the precedent set by the earlier `positions/[id]/detail/route.ts` `roundFloats` fix, which also didn't add a route-level test). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `uw-socket.ts`/`stocks-socket.ts` reconnect backoff had no jitter (follow-up audit finding, low-medium)
**Where:** `polygon-socket.ts` and `options-socket.ts` both add `Math.floor(Math.random() * 400)` jitter to their reconnect backoff delay; `uw-socket.ts`'s `scheduleReconnect()` and `stocks-socket.ts`'s `scheduleStocksReconnect()` didn't ‚Äî the delay was a plain exponential backoff with no randomization.

**Why it matters, especially now:** masked in normal single-leader operation (only one replica ever holds each socket, so there's no peer to collide with). But it compounds the split-brain fencing fix immediately above: two replicas that BOTH briefly believed they were leader (during a stall-then-fence-detection window) and got disconnected by the same upstream blip would, without jitter, reconnect at the exact same moment instead of staggered ‚Äî the opposite of what jitter exists to prevent.

**Fix:** added the identical `Math.floor(Math.random() * 400)` jitter term to both files' reconnect delay computation, matching `polygon-socket.ts`/`options-socket.ts` exactly. `uw-socket.ts`'s auth-failure cooldown branch (a fixed "wait until this deadline" cooldown, not an exponential backoff) was deliberately left unjittered ‚Äî jitter doesn't apply to a fixed-deadline wait the way it does to a churn-avoidance backoff.

**Blast radius:** the two reconnect-delay computations only ‚Äî no change to backoff caps, auth-failure cooldown logic, or any other reconnect behavior.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1013/1013` passing (no new tests ‚Äî `scheduleReconnect`/`scheduleStocksReconnect` aren't exported for direct testing, matching the precedent that `polygon-socket.ts`'s and `options-socket.ts`'s own jitter isn't unit-tested either). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî WS/cron leader locks split-brain under a stalled leader ‚Äî no fencing token (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** all 5 Redis SETNX cluster-leader locks in the codebase ‚Äî `src/lib/ws/uw-socket.ts`, `polygon-socket.ts`, `options-socket.ts`, `stocks-socket.ts`, and `src/lib/rth-warm-leader.ts` (the 5th manager fixed immediately above). Each acquires with `SET key "1" EX ttl NX` ‚Äî a **constant** value, never a per-replica identity ‚Äî then renews on a timer via an **unconditional** `EXPIRE(key, ttl)` and releases via an unconditional `DEL(key)`, neither of which ever checks that the key still belongs to the replica calling them.

**The split-brain sequence:** replica A acquires the lock. A stalls past the lock's TTL (GC pause, a slow synchronous call, event-loop backlog under load ‚Äî all normal Node.js realities, not exotic failures). The key expires in Redis. Replica B's next acquire attempt wins (`SETNX` succeeds against no key). A resumes. A's own renewal timer fires next, sees its local `isLeader` flag is still (stale) `true`, and calls `EXPIRE(key, ttl)` ‚Äî blindly re-arming the TTL on a key that now belongs to B, with no check that A still owns it. Both A and B now believe they hold leadership indefinitely (the key never naturally expires again, since both keep renewing it), with **no alert or log signal** that anything is wrong. Each of the 4 WS sockets opens its own live connection to an upstream that permits only ONE connection per API key ‚Äî both get bounced/throttled by the vendor, and `rth-warm-leader.ts` dispatches every cron-warm target from two replicas at once.

**Fix:** new `src/lib/ws/leader-lock-fencing.ts` ‚Äî each acquirer now writes a random per-process `crypto.randomUUID()` token instead of the constant `"1"`. Renew and release are now atomic Lua check-and-act scripts (`redis.eval`): `renewFencedLock` only extends the TTL if `GET(key) === myToken`, returning `false` (not just silently no-op'ing) when it isn't ‚Äî the caller then explicitly sets `isLeader = false` and logs a "lost cluster lead‚Ä¶ standing down" warning instead of continuing to believe it's leader. `releaseFencedLock` only deletes the key if it's still mine, so a stalled-then-resumed replica's shutdown path can never delete a lock a different replica has since legitimately acquired. All 5 files call the same two shared functions rather than re-deriving the check-and-act logic 5 times. Each of the 4 WS sockets already had its own leadership-gated reconcile tick (running every 10-15s, well inside every lock's 25-45s TTL) that re-checks leadership and calls the socket's `standDown()`/close ‚Äî so once the renewal detects the loss and flips the flag, the existing reconcile loop closes the now-illegitimate connection within one tick, no new teardown path needed. `rth-warm-leader.ts`'s next 60s `tick()` does the same via its own existing `!isLeader` re-acquire check.

**Blast radius:** exactly these 5 files' leader-lock acquire/renew/release call sites ‚Äî no other logic in any of them (message handling, subscription management, reconcile cadence, watchdogs) was touched. `leader-lock-fencing.ts` is a new, standalone module (only imports `node:crypto`) ‚Äî it doesn't touch `leader-lock-shared.ts`'s existing `REPLICA_COUNT` fail-open/closed policy, which is unrelated (fencing protects against a stalled-but-alive leader; the fail-open policy protects against Redis itself being unavailable ‚Äî both bugs could occur independently or together).

**Fix rationale:** a random-token-plus-Lua-check-and-act is the standard, minimal-correct fencing pattern for this exact class of lock (the well-known "Redlock safe release" shape) ‚Äî it was chosen over a full distributed-lock library (e.g. Redlock across multiple Redis instances) because this codebase already trusts a single Redis instance for these locks (see `leader-lock-shared.ts`'s own reasoning for why single-Redis SETNX is an accepted tradeoff here), so only the ownership-check gap needed closing, not the underlying single-point-of-failure model.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1009/1009` passing (5 new in `leader-lock-fencing.test.ts` ‚Äî renew succeeds/fails correctly on token match/mismatch, release deletes only on match and is a safe no-op otherwise, and token uniqueness). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `/api/market/quote` REST fallback had no negative-result cache ‚Äî sustained outage = unbounded retries + log spam (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/quote/route.ts`'s `getRestQuote()` only cached SUCCESSFUL snapshots (`quoteMem`/Redis, 5s TTL). A failed upstream call (vendor 404, timeout, empty snapshot) returned `null` with nothing cached, so the very next poll ‚Äî this route is deliberately polled every ~1.5s per open tab for the live GEX-header tape ‚Äî re-attempted the exact same upstream call. During a sustained vendor-side outage (the trigger: a benign-but-real `[market/quote] REST quote failed for SPY: ... ‚Üí 404` observed in production logs over the extended July 4th holiday weekend, traced and confirmed to be vendor snapshot-cache flakiness, not a broken endpoint/URL), every poll from every open tab on every one of 5 replicas re-hit the upstream with zero backoff ‚Äî wasted vendor-call budget for the full duration of the outage. Separately, `console.warn` fired on every single failed attempt with no rate-limiting, so a multi-hour or multi-day outage produced a wall of identical, alarming-looking log lines that gave no signal of whether this was a fresh problem or the same ongoing one.

**Fix:** added a short negative-result cache (`quoteFailureMem`, 3s TTL ‚Äî shorter than the 5s positive-cache window since a real recovery should be picked up quickly) that `getRestQuote()` checks before even attempting L1/L2/upstream, so a ticker mid-outage returns `{available:false}` immediately without touching the upstream. Paired with `quoteFailureWarned`, a per-ticker "already logged this outage" set: the first failure after a success logs one `console.warn`; every subsequent failure while still in the outage window is silent; the warning re-arms only once a success clears both maps. Net effect: one log line per outage (not one per poll), and upstream call volume during a sustained outage drops to roughly 1 per ticker per 3s cluster-wide instead of 1 per ticker per ~1.5s per open tab per replica.

**Blast radius:** `getRestQuote()` only ‚Äî the WS path (`indexStore` direct read) and the positive-cache path are both unchanged. `{available:false}` was already the exact response shape on any failure before this fix; callers see no contract change, just fewer redundant upstream calls and quieter logs during a real outage.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1007/1007` passing (3 new in a new `route.test.ts` for this route, using `mock.module()` to stub the upstream/auth/cache dependencies per the pattern established in `platform/intel/route.test.ts`: a failed snapshot returns `available:false` and logs exactly once; a second poll for the same ticker within the negative-cache window neither re-hits the upstream nor re-warns; a different ticker's success is unaffected by another ticker's failure cache). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî 9 more hand-rolled ET-date duplicates found consolidating the 4 the audit flagged (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** the follow-up audit flagged 4 files (`spx-play-engine.ts:851`, `spx-signals.ts:80`, `nighthawk/agents/day-trade-filters.ts:90`, `nighthawk/hunt-builder.ts:87`) still hand-rolling `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` instead of importing `todayEt()` from `et-date.ts`. Before fixing just those 4, grepped the whole codebase for the exact same literal pattern to get real blast-radius coverage (per this repo's PR-writeup policy: fix and note every call site touched by the same root cause, not just the one flagged) ‚Äî found **5 more** in `greek-exposure-summary.ts:33`, `providers/polygon.ts:226`, `providers/macro-events.ts` (3 separate call sites: `:237`, `:259`, `:396`), `api/cron/nighthawk-edition/route.ts:57`, `api/cron/nighthawk-morning-confirm/route.ts:142`, and `components/desk/GexHeatmap.tsx:2665` (a client component ‚Äî safe to consolidate since `et-date.ts`'s header explicitly documents it as "importable from server engines/stores AND from client modules").

**Fix:** all 9 sites now call `todayEt()` (aliased where a file already had its own local `todayEt` variable name or a colliding same-named import from `nighthawk/session.ts` ‚Äî see Fix rationale). Two files (`providers/polygon.ts`, `providers/macro-events.ts`) already imported `todayEtYmd`/`todayEt` from the earlier consolidation for OTHER call sites in the same file but had these specific lines missed ‚Äî a reminder that "the file already imports the helper" doesn't guarantee every call site in it uses it.

**Fix rationale ‚Äî naming collisions handled per-file:**
- `nighthawk/agents/day-trade-filters.ts` and `nighthawk/hunt-builder.ts` each had a local `const todayEt = ...` variable ‚Äî imported the shared function under an alias (`import { todayEt as todayEtStr }`) so the local variable name (and every downstream reference to it in the same function) stayed unchanged.
- `api/cron/nighthawk-morning-confirm/route.ts` already imports a **different, zero-argument** `todayEt` from `@/lib/nighthawk/session` (itself a thin wrapper delegating to the same canonical `et-date.ts` implementation) ‚Äî but this call site needed the parameterized form (`todayEt(new Date(ms))`, converting an arbitrary bar timestamp, not "today"). Importing the real `todayEt` under a second identifier (`import { todayEt as etYmdOf }`) avoided a duplicate-import compile error while preserving the existing zero-arg call sites elsewhere in the same file untouched.
- `api/cron/nighthawk-edition/route.ts` already imports the *same* correctly-delegating `todayEt` from `nighthawk/session.ts` with a compatible zero-arg call shape ‚Äî no new import needed, the raw inline computation was simply replaced with a call to what was already in scope.

**Noted but deliberately NOT fixed in this pass:** `nighthawk/session.ts` also defines its own `formatEtDate(d: Date)`, which independently reimplements the identical `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone: ET})` computation as a named (not raw inline) helper ‚Äî functionally redundant with `todayEt(d)` from `et-date.ts` now that `todayEt` accepts an optional `Date` argument. This wasn't included here because it's an established, multi-consumer named export (not a raw inline duplicate), and removing/aliasing it is a slightly bigger refactor (auditing every `formatEtDate` call site) that deserves its own focused pass rather than scope-creeping into this fix.

**Blast radius:** exactly the 9 call sites listed above, across 8 files ‚Äî no function signature or return type changed anywhere, so no downstream consumer needed updating.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (confirms no naming collisions slipped through); full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests ‚Äî every substitution is a byte-identical drop-in, matching the same class of change already covered by `et-date.ts`'s own test suite from the original consolidation). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî 9th `fmtPremium` reimplementation found, in the file that IS the grounding-guard reference implementation (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/gex-heatmap/explain/route.ts:44` ‚Äî a local `fmtMoney(n: number)` reimplementing the "compact signed dollar magnitude" formatter that task #75 (earlier today) already consolidated 8 other copies of into `src/lib/fmt-money.ts`'s `fmtPremium()`. This is the route that builds the Largo "desk read" narrative prompt context and then grounds the model's response against it via `checkNumbersGrounded` ‚Äî i.e. the numbers this formatter renders are exactly what the model is told is true AND what its output gets checked against. A silently-diverging formatter here doesn't just risk a wrong number on screen; it risks the grounding check itself passing or failing against the wrong reference string.

**A real behavioral divergence, not just a style copy:** the local version always used `.toFixed(1)` in its thousands branch (e.g. `$15.0K`); the canonical `fmtPremium` uses `k < 10 ? k.toFixed(1) : k.toFixed(0)` (whole-K at $10K+, e.g. `$15K`) ‚Äî confirmed by reading `fmt-money.ts`'s own comments, which explain this exact branch was itself a deliberate fix for an earlier bug (`GexDealerPanel.tsx:39` printing `$5000.0M` instead of `$5.0B` before the billions-first branch ordering was added). The local copy also had no null/NaN guard (`fmtPremium` returns `"‚Äî"` for `null`/non-finite input; the local one had no `null` case in its signature at all and would have silently rendered `"$0"` for a NaN via `Math.abs(NaN)` ‚Üí `0` had one ever reached it).

**Fix:** deleted the local `fmtMoney`; both call sites (top flow strikes by net premium, dark-pool levels by notional) now call `fmtPremium` imported from `@/lib/fmt-money`.

**Blast radius:** 2 call sites, both within this route's own prompt-context builder ‚Äî no other file imports this route's (now-deleted) local `fmtMoney`.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests ‚Äî `fmtPremium` already has direct coverage in `fmt-money.test.ts` from task #75, and this route has no existing test file to extend). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî WS-fed `change_pct` served unrounded via `/api/market/quote` (follow-up audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/ws/polygon-socket.ts` ‚Äî both places `indexStore[sym].change_pct` is computed from a live WS message (the `A`/`AM` aggregate-bar handler, and the `V` tick-value handler) did raw floating-point division with no rounding: `((current - sessionOpen) / sessionOpen) * 100`. Every REST sibling in `src/lib/providers/polygon.ts` rounds the same computation via `Number((...).toFixed(2))` ‚Äî this WS-fed path was the one place that didn't. `src/app/api/market/quote/route.ts` reads `indexStore` straight through into its JSON response with no `roundFloats()` pass, so the raw unrounded float reached the wire. This is the SPX/VIX header tape `GexHeatmap.tsx` polls every ~1.5s ‚Äî previously masked only by the frontend's own `fmtPct()` display formatting, i.e. correct on screen but wrong in the actual API payload (the same "systemic: several endpoints serve unrounded floats" pattern this doc's CLAUDE.md note calls out).

**Fix:** extracted the shared computation into a new exported `computeSessionChangePct(current, sessionOpen)` in `polygon-socket.ts`, rounding via the same `Number((...).toFixed(2))` pattern as the REST sibling, and pointed both the `A`/`AM` and `V` handlers at it instead of each inlining (and, in the `V` handler's case, never rounding) the arithmetic separately.

**Blast radius:** both `indexStore` write sites in `polygon-socket.ts` ‚Äî no consumer of `indexStore` or `/api/market/quote` needed a change, since the field's type/shape is unchanged (still a `number`), only its precision.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1008/1008` passing (4 new in `polygon-socket-change-pct.test.ts` ‚Äî rounds a representative raw float to 2dp, returns 0 with no anchor, rounds a negative change correctly, and a general "never more than 2 decimal digits" property check). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `unusual-whales.ts` had its own unenumerated ET-date duplicate, largest blast radius of any date-dup found (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/providers/unusual-whales.ts:346` ‚Äî a local `todayIso()` reimplementing the exact `Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` logic that task #74 (earlier today, and originally on 2026-07-01/02) consolidated 6 other copies of into `src/lib/et-date.ts`'s `todayEt()` ‚Äî but this copy was never found or enumerated, because it lives in the core UW provider file rather than in any of the play-engine/dashboard files the original sweep scanned. It has 6 call sites (`:373`, `:463`, `:821`, `:881`, `:924`, `:1495`) gating 0DTE expiry-date filtering and "today's" max-pain contract selection ‚Äî the largest blast radius of any date-duplication instance found across either audit pass, since `unusual-whales.ts` is the shared REST client every 0DTE/GEX-by-strike/max-pain consumer platform-wide ultimately calls through.

**Why it's a real risk, not just style:** `et-date.ts`'s own header comment states the exact failure mode this class of duplication causes ‚Äî a future one-off DST or timezone-boundary fix applied to only one copy silently shifts that copy's day-boundary out of sync with every other copy, corrupting cross-file date comparisons (e.g. "is this contract's expiry today" agreeing in one file but not another) without any error being thrown.

**Fix:** deleted the local `todayIso()` and its 6 call sites now call `todayEt()` imported from `@/lib/et-date`. Confirmed byte-identical output before changing anything: `new Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York", year:"numeric", month:"2-digit", day:"2-digit"})` (the local version's explicit options) and `new Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", {timeZone:"America/New_York"})` (`todayEt()`'s, no explicit y/m/d fields) both format to the same `YYYY-MM-DD` string ‚Äî verified directly in a Node REPL against the current date rather than assumed from reading the two implementations.

**Blast radius:** single file, 6 call sites, all within `unusual-whales.ts` itself ‚Äî no caller of any of these functions passes or receives a date string differently than before (the return shape/format is identical), so no downstream consumer needed a change.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `1004/1004` passing (no new tests needed ‚Äî the substitution is a proven byte-identical drop-in, and `todayEt()` itself already has direct coverage from task #74's consolidation). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` clean.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî 5th WS-adjacent leader-lock manager (`rth-warm-leader.ts`) missed by the REPLICA_COUNT fail-open sweep (follow-up audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/rth-warm-leader.ts:47-56` (`tryAcquireLead`) ‚Äî `if (!redis) return true; // single-replica / no Redis ‚Äî run locally`. This is the exact fail-open-on-Redis-loss bug already fixed today in all four WS socket managers (`uw-socket.ts`/`polygon-socket.ts`/`options-socket.ts`/`stocks-socket.ts`, see the "Gate WS leader-lock fail-open" entry below), but `rth-warm-leader.ts` wasn't in that sweep's file list ‚Äî it lives outside `src/lib/ws/` and isn't itself a WebSocket, so a `grep`-by-directory or by-name pass over "the WS sockets" walks right past it. It's booted from the same `ensureDataSockets()` entry point as the four already-fixed files (`src/lib/ws/init-data-sockets.ts`) and races the same Redis `SET NX EX` leader-election pattern.

**Impact:** on a Redis outage across the 5-replica production topology, every replica would simultaneously believe it holds the cluster lead and independently poll `cron_job_runs` + dispatch `nights-watch-warm`/`uw-cache-refresh`/`heatmap-warm` warmers every 60s. Bounded (the dispatch targets are curated idempotent-only per `cron-dispatch.ts`) so this isn't data-corrupting, but it's 5x redundant vendor-facing warm calls landing exactly when the WS layer is *also* degrading ‚Äî the worst possible moment to add uncoordinated load, and the fix for the sibling bug specifically exists to prevent that compounding effect.

**Fix:** identical pattern to the four already-fixed sockets ‚Äî reused `wsLeaderShouldFailOpenWithoutRedis()`/`alertWsLeaderFailClosedOnce()`/`clearWsLeaderFailClosedAlert()` from the shared `src/lib/ws/leader-lock-shared.ts` module added earlier today, rather than duplicating the REPLICA_COUNT-threshold logic a 5th time. `tryAcquireLead()` now fails open only when `REPLICA_COUNT<=1`; otherwise fails closed (with a one-time ops alert) on both the "no Redis client" and the "Redis errored" branches ‚Äî the errored-branch behavior is slightly stricter than before (previously always failed closed on error regardless of replica count; now correctly fails open too at `REPLICA_COUNT<=1`, matching the sibling sockets).

**Blast radius:** searched the rest of the codebase for the same `SET ... NX` leader-election shape (`cf-purge-on-deploy.ts`, `membership-sync-limit.ts`, `webhook/whop/route.ts` also matched) ‚Äî all three are deliberately-scoped, already-correct fail-open designs for a *different* problem class (idempotent one-shot cache purge, per-user rate-limit cooldown, webhook dedup) where fail-open means "occasionally redundant/duplicate work," not "N-way contention for a single exclusive upstream resource." None needed the same fix; `rth-warm-leader.ts` was the only other genuine cluster-leader-election lock in the codebase.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; existing `rth-warm-leader.test.ts` (covers `rthWriterOverdue`) and `leader-lock-shared.test.ts` (covers the fail-open/closed threshold itself) both pass unchanged ‚Äî `tryAcquireLead` isn't exported for direct unit testing, matching the precedent set by the four sibling socket files fixed earlier today (none of them export their `tryAcquire*Lead` either; the shared threshold logic they all now call is what's actually under test). `npm run build` clean.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Largo answer-grounding cron false-flagged every recent answer (ops-auto-fix #444, P0)
**Where:** `src/lib/correctness/largo-verifier.ts` shipped a bespoke `extractNumericTokens` regex (separate from the runtime Layer-4 verifier in `src/lib/bie/verifier.ts`) that false-flagged prod Largo answers: list markers (`- 8 alerts` ‚Üí `-8`), money-suffix bleed (`$80 max pain` ‚Üí `$80M` = 80,000,000 via trailing `m` in "max"), EMA period refs (`50-EMA` ‚Üí 50), date fragments (`Jul 10` ‚Üí 10), and flagged ANY single ungrounded token instead of using the same coverage threshold `largo-terminal.ts` applies before appending the runtime caution footer. Result: `data-correctness` cron failed with `3/3 recent Largo answers cited a number absent from tool-call results`, cascading to cron-staleness-watchdog P1.

**Fix:** new shared `auditLargoAnswerGrounding()` in `src/lib/bie/verifier.ts` ‚Äî reuses `extractNumericClaims` + `verifyClaims` (identical to in-turn Layer 4) and flags only when `total >= 4 && coverage < 0.5` AND the answer lacks the `_BIE verification:` runtime caution footer (undisclosed low coverage). `largo-verifier.ts` now calls this instead of the bespoke regex path.

**Blast radius:** cron audit path only ‚Äî runtime Largo behavior unchanged; answers that already disclosed low coverage via the footer are not re-flagged by the cron.

**Verification:** 4 new tests in `src/lib/bie/largo-grounding-fixture.test.ts` (invented-target fixture, footer skip, list-marker non-flag, `$80 max pain` non-flag); replay against prod rows #508/#510/#512 ‚Üí 0/3 flagged (was 3/3).

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `PG_POOL_MAX` √ó `REPLICA_COUNT` oversubscribes PgBouncer's documented backend budget 3.75x (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/db.ts:119` ‚Äî `max: parseInt(process.env.PG_POOL_MAX ?? "5", 10)`. Production explicitly sets `PG_POOL_MAX=15` (Railway service env var) across 5 live replicas (`docs/PGBOUNCER-SETUP.md`), for **75** total client connections against PgBouncer's own documented `DEFAULT_POOL_SIZE=20` Postgres-backend budget ‚Äî a real 3.75x oversubscription. The 2026-07-03 "Query read timeout" investigation into an admin-endpoint failure storm modeled the ceiling using the code DEFAULT (5√ó5=25) instead of the documented production override (15√ó5=75), understating the real ceiling by 3x and never cross-referencing `PGBOUNCER-SETUP.md`'s own numbers ‚Äî see that entry's 2026-07-04 update below for the correction. There was also no runtime visibility into pool contention (`getDatabasePoolStats().waiting`, which already existed) anywhere in the admin health snapshot/alert path ‚Äî a replica queuing queries behind a full pool had no signal short of the timeout itself firing.

**Fix, three parts, matching the audit's exact fix instruction:**
1. **Safer, computed default:** `src/lib/db.ts` now computes `PG_POOL_MAX`'s *fallback* from the documented PgBouncer budget √∑ `REPLICA_COUNT` (`computeSafePgPoolMaxDefault`, both env-overridable via `PGBOUNCER_DEFAULT_POOL_SIZE`/`REPLICA_COUNT`) instead of a flat, uncoupled guess ‚Äî at the current 5-replica topology that's 4/replica, not the previous flat default of 5. An explicit `PG_POOL_MAX` env var is still honored as-is (never silently overridden ‚Äî this is a production knob an operator set on purpose), but if the explicit value √ó `REPLICA_COUNT` would still exceed the documented budget, a startup warning now logs the exact numbers instead of the risk staying invisible.
2. **Visibility:** `getDatabasePoolStats()` (already existed, already exposed to the admin dashboard's raw JSON) is now also read by `buildAdminHealthSnapshot()` ‚Äî `waiting > 0` surfaces as a `warning`-severity issue (contention forming), escalating to `critical` (and gating `health_ok`) only when `waiting >= total` (the pool is genuinely saturated, not just momentarily queued behind a burst), mirroring the existing `redis_degraded` synthetic-issue pattern in the same function.
3. **Doc cross-reference:** updated the 2026-07-03 FINDINGS.md entry (see below) to correct the understated ceiling and point at this fix.

**Action needed (user, cannot be done from a PR):** the *default* is now correct, but production's **explicit** `PG_POOL_MAX=15` Railway env var still overrides it and will keep logging the new oversubscription warning until changed. Lower it to `4` (or raise PgBouncer's `DEFAULT_POOL_SIZE` with headroom, per the audit's stated alternative) in the Railway dashboard for `blackout-web`. Not applied directly from this session despite working Railway API access ‚Äî flipping a live production database connection-pool setting is exactly the class of hard-to-reverse, shared-infrastructure change this repo's operating guidance says to surface rather than silently apply, same posture as the P0 Postgres-credential-rotation finding earlier this week.

**Blast radius:** `src/lib/db.ts`'s pool-construction call site only (the `max` value it computes); `src/lib/admin-health.ts`'s `buildAdminHealthSnapshot()` gains one new field (`db_pool`) and one new synthetic-issue branch, following the exact shape already established for `redis_degraded`. No other consumer of either function was touched.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite passing (4 new in `db.test.ts` for `computeSafePgPoolMaxDefault`: divides the documented budget across replicas, clamps to a floor of 1 for absurd replica counts, and the replicaCount<=1 no-op case). `npm run build` clean ‚Äî note: initially wired the env-reading helper via the existing `provider-rate-limiter-shared.ts`, which broke `next build` (its dynamic `import("@/lib/redis-pubsub")` drags `ioredis`/`node:diagnostics_channel` into any edge-runtime bundle that transitively imports `db.ts`); fixed by inlining the one-line helper directly in `db.ts` instead of sharing it. `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Admin rate-quota headroom read ~1/REPLICA_COUNT of true API usage (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/api-rate-quotas.ts:33` (`buildRateQuotaHeadroom`) computes `used`/`pct`/`status` purely from whatever call-count map it's handed. `admin-api-dashboard.ts:370` fed it exclusively from `getCallsByProvider1m()` ‚Äî a per-process, module-level in-memory counter (`api-telemetry.ts`'s `events` array, capped at `MAX_EVENTS=800`) that only ever sees calls made by *that one replica*. Production runs 5 replicas (per `docs/PGBOUNCER-SETUP.md`), so the panel structurally read roughly a fifth of true vendor call volume ‚Äî it could show "ok" headroom for Unusual Whales/Polygon/Anthropic rate limits right up to (and during) an actual cluster-wide rate-limit event, the exact failure mode the panel exists to catch. The fix ingredients already existed two lines away: `admin-api-dashboard.ts:296-297` already fetches `crossTelemetry = await readCrossInstanceTelemetry()` (Redis-backed, genuinely cluster-wide) and its `providers[id].calls_5m` was already used for the headline 5m totals a few lines further down ‚Äî `rateHeadroom` was just built before that data was reconciled, and never wired to it.

**Fix:** new `deriveClusterCallsByProvider1m(clusterProviders, localCallsByProvider1m)` in `api-rate-quotas.ts` converts the cluster-wide 5-minute rollup (`calls_5m`) into a per-minute-equivalent count (`Math.round(calls_5m / 5)`) keyed by provider, and falls back to the caller's local per-replica counts when cross-instance telemetry is unavailable (e.g. Redis down) ‚Äî degraded but never null. `admin-api-dashboard.ts` now calls this before building `rateHeadroom`, feeding it `crossTelemetry?.providers` alongside the existing local snapshot as the fallback.

**Blast radius:** single call site (`admin-api-dashboard.ts:370`) ‚Äî `buildRateQuotaHeadroom`'s own per-provider pct/status math is unchanged, only its input source changed. No other consumer of `getCallsByProvider1m()` was touched (the headline-totals logic a few lines below already had its own correct cluster-vs-local branching for the 5m-window case and was left alone).

**Fix rationale:** dividing the already-correct 5-minute cluster rollup by 5 was chosen over widening `PROVIDER_RATE_QUOTAS` to a 5-minute quota because it required no change to the quota table or the `status` thresholds (`ok`/`warn`/`critical`) that admins are already calibrated to reading as "per-minute" ‚Äî the rollup's own 5m window is simply an artifact of how `api-telemetry-redis.ts` batches cross-instance writes, not a meaningful quota boundary. Falling back to local counts (rather than showing nothing) was deliberately kept so the panel degrades gracefully instead of going blank when Redis is down, matching the honesty pattern used elsewhere in this file (never silently show a healthier number than reality, but never hard-fail a display panel either).

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `993/993` passing (5 new in `api-rate-quotas.test.ts` ‚Äî converts a 5m rollup to per-minute, falls back on null/undefined cluster telemetry, treats a missing `calls_5m` as zero, and two existing-behavior regression checks on `buildRateQuotaHeadroom` itself). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Largo's numeric-grounding verifier had no real data to run against ‚Äî tool-call results were never persisted (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/correctness/largo-verifier.ts` shipped real grounding machinery (`extractNumericTokens`/`collectResultNumbers`/`traceNumbersToResults`) but could only self-test it on a hardcoded fixture: Largo's persistence (`largo_messages`) retained the assistant ANSWER TEXT and TOOL NAMES only ‚Äî the tool-call RESULTS (the actual ground truth needed to trace a past answer's numbers back to source) lived only in-memory inside `anthropicToolLoop` and were discarded after the turn. There was also no cross-user "list recent answers" reader (`fetchLargoMessagesPublic` requires both `sessionId` AND the owning `userId`), so even if results were logged, the cron couldn't enumerate them.

**Fix:** three-part, matching the audit's exact fix instruction.
1. **Schema:** additive `ALTER TABLE largo_messages ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS tool_results JSONB` (nullable ‚Äî no backfill possible for existing history, and BIE-router answers with zero tool calls correctly stay `NULL` rather than `'[]'`).
2. **Write path:** `appendLargoMessage()` now accepts an optional `toolResults` param and persists it; `largo-terminal.ts`'s two Claude-tool-loop paths (`runLargoQuery`, `runLargoQueryStream`) now pass their already-built `capturedResults` array (previously built at runtime and simply discarded ‚Äî `largo-terminal.ts:306`/`421`) into the assistant-message write. The BIE-router fast path (no tool calls, `routed.context` instead) is intentionally untouched.
3. **Read path + verifier:** new `fetchRecentLargoAnswersWithResults(limit=50)` in `largo-store.ts` ‚Äî a bounded, cross-user, cron-readable reader (assistant rows only, `tool_results IS NOT NULL`) closing the "not enumerable" gap. `verifyLargo()` now calls it and runs the SAME self-tested engine against real answers: `pass` when every answer's numbers trace to that turn's tool results, `flag` (with example ungrounded values) when any don't, and a clearly-labeled `consistency-only` "no data yet" note (never a false green) for the transitional period right after this migration deploys before any new Largo turns have run.

**Blast radius:** none to existing Largo behavior ‚Äî `capturedResults` was already being built every turn for the existing Layer-4 `verifyClaims` in-answer caveat (task #87 territory); this only adds a second, durable write of the same already-computed data. No new upstream calls, no new provider fan-out ‚Äî the verifier's real-data check is one bounded DB read of already-logged rows.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `988/988` passing (3 new in a new `largo-store.test.ts`, using `mock.module()` on `@/lib/db` to assert the reader's SQL filters correctly and maps rows/defaults safely). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. `largo-verifier.ts` itself has no direct test ‚Äî it (like its sibling verifiers `desk-verifier.ts`/`heatmap-verifier.ts`) starts with `import "server-only"`, which throws immediately when the file is imported outside Next.js's server-component runtime, making it fundamentally untestable via the plain `node --test` runner used here ‚Äî this matches the established, pre-existing pattern for every file in `src/lib/correctness/`, confirmed by trying the direct-import approach first and hitting exactly that crash (same failure class discovered on `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts` in task #79, but there via a transitive import rather than a direct one).

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Night Hawk critic cut/downgraded plays on unverified self-reported reasons (audit finding, medium ‚Äî last of the 7 LLM-surface grounding fixes)
**Where:** `src/lib/nighthawk/play-critic.ts`'s `critiquePlays()` cuts or downgrades a play based solely on Claude's self-reported `reason` string, with no check that the cited contradiction is real against the play's own thesis/entry/target/stop/dossier data. A hallucinated "contradicts X" reason could silently zero a genuinely good play with no way to catch it.

**Fix:** applied the shared guard, per-play rather than batch-wide. Captured each play's own prompt text block (`--- Play #N ---` / thesis / entry / target / stop / options / dossier) into a `knownTextByRank` map while building the prompt, so a verdict's reason is checked against exactly what THAT play's block showed Claude ‚Äî not the whole batch's combined prompt (a reason for play #3 citing a number that only appears in play #7's block is still ungrounded for #3). `checkNumbersGrounded(verdict.reason, extractNumbersFromText(knownTextByRank.get(play.rank)))` now gates every `cut`/`downgrade` verdict (a `keep` verdict has no consequence, so it isn't gated); an ungrounded reason gets the verdict REJECTED ‚Äî the play survives unchanged, with a note recording the rejection (`notes` is durably persisted into `nighthawk_editions.meta.critic_notes` per this audit's own earlier finding, so the rejection itself is part of the audit trail, not silently dropped).

**Blast radius:** none to existing behavior ‚Äî a grounded cut/downgrade (the expected case when the critic is actually right) is applied exactly as before; only a hallucinated verdict now gets rejected instead of silently executing.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `985/985` passing (4 new in a new `play-critic.test.ts`, using `node:test`'s `mock.module()` on `../providers/anthropic` ‚Äî an established pattern already used in `platform-intel-snapshot.test.ts` ‚Äî to control the critic's mocked response and assert: a grounded cut applies, an ungrounded cut is rejected with conviction/rank unchanged, an ungrounded downgrade is rejected, and a `keep` verdict is never gated regardless of its reason's content); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

**This completes the audit's numeric-grounding fabrication-guard work** across all 7 flagged LLM narrative surfaces (`gex-heatmap/explain` already had it; `spx-play-claude.ts`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`, `flow-brief/route.ts`, `nights-watch/position-narrative.ts`, `nighthawk/play-critic.ts` fixed across tasks #76-82), sharing one `src/lib/grounding-guard.ts` module (`checkNumbersGrounded`, `collectKnownNumbers`, `extractNumbersFromText`) instead of 7 independent, potentially-drifting implementations.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Night's Watch per-position AI narrative had no fabrication check (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/nights-watch/position-narrative.ts`'s `buildPositionNarrative()` caches and returns Claude's per-position desk narrative (Greeks, P&L, levels, dealer positioning) with grounding enforced only by prompt instruction ("NEVER invent or estimate a price, level, Greek, premium, percentage, or date"), never structurally verified.

**Fix:** applied the shared guard. Like `flow-brief` and `play-explainer`, this function's prompt (`buildContext(detail)`) is a single plain-text string built from verified fields (position, Greeks, dealer gamma, flow, technicals, catalysts, confluence ‚Äî every missing value already forced to `"n/a"`, never a placeholder number), so `extractNumbersFromText(context)` is the "known good" set. After generation, `checkNumbersGrounded(out, extractNumbersFromText(context))` runs before caching; on failure it returns `null` **without caching** ‚Äî mirroring the function's own pre-existing behavior for empty output (`if (!out) return null; // not cached ‚Üí next open retries`), so the caller falls back to the deterministic `whatToDo` for this request and the next detail-open gets a fresh attempt, rather than pinning a discarded narrative's absence for the full 5-minute TTL.

**Blast radius:** none to existing behavior ‚Äî a grounded narrative (the common case) is unaffected; a hallucinated one now falls back to the deterministic `whatToDo` exactly as the file's own header comment already promises for every other failure mode ("Fails OPEN... ‚Üí null, and the caller falls back to the deterministic whatToDo").

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `981/981` passing (2 new in a new `position-narrative.test.ts`, exercising `buildContext` + the shared guard against a grounded vs. hallucinated narrative using a hand-built `PositionDetail` fixture); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. Exported `buildContext` (previously module-local) for testability ‚Äî confirmed safe (unlike `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`, this file has no transitive `"server-only"` import in its dependency chain).

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Shared 15-minute flow-brief memo had no fabrication check (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/flow-brief/route.ts`'s `GET` handler cached Claude's flow-tape summary for a shared 15-minute window (served to every user) with zero check that cited dollar figures/tickers matched the actual alerts/dark-prints it was given.

**Fix:** applied the shared guard. Unlike the two prior fixes, this route's prompt (`buildPrompt()`) is already a single plain-text string (not a structured object serialized via `JSON.stringify`), so the "known good" set is simply `extractNumbersFromText(prompt)` ‚Äî every number literally present in the exact text Claude was shown. After generation, `checkNumbersGrounded(trimmed, extractNumbersFromText(prompt))` runs; on failure, the cached result explicitly stores `brief: null` for that window (not a thrown error). This deliberately differs from the `spx-commentary.ts` fix (#429), which throws to skip caching entirely and force an immediate retryable 502: `serverCache`'s `refreshCache()` caches whatever a factory *returns* (including a bare `null`) regardless of value ‚Äî it's throwing that's the "don't cache" signal. A retry within the same 15-minute window would see identical flow data and likely hallucinate the same way again, so caching `brief: null` for the rest of the window (matching this route's existing "no flow data ‚Üí cached null" behavior) is more useful than forcing a wasted immediate re-generation.

**Blast radius:** none to existing behavior ‚Äî grounded briefs (the overwhelming common case) are unaffected; only a hallucinated brief now degrades to `brief: null` for its window instead of shipping the fabricated line.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `979/979` passing (no new tests ‚Äî `buildPrompt`/`normalizeDark` are route-file-local functions and Next.js route modules only permit the fixed `GET`/`POST`/`dynamic`/etc. export set, confirmed earlier this audit on `/api/ready`'s `redisStatus` export attempt ‚Äî so they can't be exported for direct testing without a larger refactor moving them to a separate lib file, which was out of scope here; coverage relies on the already-comprehensive `checkNumbersGrounded`/`extractNumbersFromText` tests in `grounding-guard.test.ts`, same precedent as `spx-play-claude.ts`/`spx-commentary.ts`); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Night Hawk "Full Hawk Intel" briefing's success path shipped Claude prose unchecked (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`'s `generatePlayExplanation()` only fell back to the deterministic, grounded `buildGroundedPlayExplanationFallback()` when generation failed OUTRIGHT (empty response after 45s timeout) ‚Äî a fluent but hallucinated NON-EMPTY briefing passed straight through to the member-visible "Full Hawk Intel" panel unchecked.

**Fix:** the prompt's source data arrives as 3 already-formatted TEXT blocks (market recap, play card, ticker dossier) rather than a structured object ‚Äî the dossier in particular is a free-text string from `formatTickerDossierText()`, where a real level can appear embedded in prose like `"$182.50/share"` or `"6020-6030"`. `collectKnownNumbers` (task #78, walks object/array leaves) can't see numbers embedded in strings, so added `extractNumbersFromText(text)` to the shared `grounding-guard.ts` module: unfiltered regex extraction of every bare numeric token from free text (as opposed to `checkNumbersGrounded`'s filtered extraction, which is judging the GENERATED text and deliberately skips %/money/small-ints). After a non-empty generation, `checkNumbersGrounded(briefing, extractNumbersFromText(marketRecapBlock + playBlock + dossierContext))` ‚Äî the exact 3 blocks the prompt was built from ‚Äî now runs before the briefing is returned; on failure it falls back to the same grounded card fallback already used for the failure path.

**Blast radius:** `extractNumbersFromText` is a second new reusable primitive in the shared grounding module (alongside `collectKnownNumbers`) for the remaining LLM-surface tasks wherever the "known good" source is free text rather than a structured object.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `979/979` passing (3 new in `grounding-guard.test.ts` for `extractNumbersFromText`, 2 new in `play-explainer.test.ts` exercising the exact grounding mechanism against a grounded vs. hallucinated briefing). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. Note: `play-explainer.test.ts`'s new tests build the "known" text from `buildGroundedPlayExplanationFallback()` (same numeric content as the real play-card block) rather than importing `play-explainer.ts` directly ‚Äî that module transitively imports `"server-only"` (via `fetchTickerDossier` ‚Üí provider chain), which throws outside the Next.js server-component runtime and would crash the plain `node --test` runner.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî SPX Claude play-gate thesis had no fabrication guard; zero durable audit trail (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/spx-play-claude.ts`'s `evaluateClaudePlayApproval()` splices Claude's free-text `thesis` verbatim into real-money 0DTE play cards (member-visible, via `spx-play-engine.ts`) with no check that any level it cites is real ‚Äî grounding was prompt-instruction only ("cite MTF + S/R + flow + news"), never verified. The Claude-gated pipeline also had zero durable audit-log write path: the verdict that gates a live entry (APPROVE_BUY or VETO) was cached in-memory/Redis for reuse but never recorded anywhere queryable after the fact ‚Äî a disputed trade could never be traced back to what Claude actually said and why.

**Fix:** added `knownPlayLevels(desk, confluence, technicals)` ‚Äî every price level actually fed into the Claude prompt (price/vwap/hod/lod/pdh/pdl/gamma_flip/gex_king/max_pain/support-resistance levels/GEX wall strikes/confluence entry-stop-target/multi-timeframe closes), mirroring `gex-heatmap/explain`'s `knownPriceLevels()` pattern. After Claude's JSON response parses successfully, `checkNumbersGrounded(result.thesis, known)` (the shared guard from task #76) now runs before the verdict is used or cached; an ungrounded thesis discards the ENTIRE Claude verdict (not just the prose) and falls back to `mechanicalVerdict()` ‚Äî the same fail-closed philosophy this function already applies to every other failure mode (Claude unconfigured, budget exceeded, generation failed). Also added `logPlayVerdict()`, a best-effort, fire-and-forget write to the existing `alert_audit_log` table (via `insertAlertAuditLog`, `alert_type: "spx_claude_play"`) capturing `{verdict, confidence: confluence.score, thesis}` plus the deterministic confluence grade/score ‚Äî called for both the grounded-approved Claude verdict and the grounding-failure-forced mechanical fallback (the two cases that represent "the verdict that gated the trade").

**Scope note:** did not instrument the function's earlier fail-closed branches (Claude unconfigured, gate disabled, budget exceeded, raw generation failed) ‚Äî those are already self-explanatory operational states, not "Claude's judgment on this play," and the audit finding's `{verdict, confidence, thesis}` shape only makes sense once Claude has actually produced a verdict. Kept the fix scoped to the two paths where a Claude-influenced trading decision is actually made.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `970/970` passing (5 new, covering `knownPlayLevels`'s field extraction and the grounding-guard integration with both a grounded and a hallucinated thesis); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. (Full async pipeline ‚Äî Claude calls, DB caching ‚Äî not mocked/tested; no existing test harness for that in this file's sibling `spx-play-*.test.ts` files.)
