## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Flagship SPX Live Desk AI commentary had no fabrication guard (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/providers/spx-commentary.ts`'s `generateSpxCommentary()` returns Claude's parsed JSON narrative (`headline` + `body`) directly, then the caller (`src/app/api/market/spx/commentary/route.ts`) cluster-caches it for a full 5-minute window and serves it to every connected premium user ‚Äî with zero post-generation check that any cited number is real, unlike the sibling `gex-heatmap/explain` route. The file's own header comment (pre-fix) documents a prior real incident of exactly this failure class ("the bug where raw millions got mislabeled 'B' from a stale prompt example").

**Fix:** applied the shared guard from task #76. Since the prompt's `ctx` object (the `CURRENT DESK SNAPSHOT (JSON)` block Claude is given) is large and deeply nested ‚Äî price action, moving averages, dealer GEX, GEX walls, flow-by-expiry, sector heat, mag7 greek flow, macro indicators, etc. ‚Äî hand-enumerating every legitimate numeric field (the approach used for `gex-heatmap/explain` and `spx-play-claude.ts`) risked missing one and false-positive-blocking a legitimate commentary. Instead added `collectKnownNumbers(value)` to the shared `grounding-guard.ts` module: a recursive tree-walker (same spirit as the existing `roundFloats()` utility) that collects every finite number anywhere in an arbitrary JSON-like value. After Claude's response parses successfully, `checkNumbersGrounded(`${headline}\n${body}`, collectKnownNumbers(ctx))` runs before the result is returned; on failure, `generateSpxCommentary` returns `null` instead of a fallback narrative ‚Äî the caller already treats a `null` return exactly like a generation failure (throws, `serverCache` skips its store, nothing is cached, the route returns a retryable 502). No new fallback logic needed since the existing error path was already the correct one.

**Blast radius:** `collectKnownNumbers` is a new, independently-reusable primitive in the shared grounding module (not spx-commentary-specific) ‚Äî it will also serve the remaining LLM-surface tasks (#79-82) wherever a guard needs to ground against a whole context object rather than a hand-picked field list.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `970/970` passing (4 new in `grounding-guard.test.ts` covering `collectKnownNumbers`'s recursive walk, null/NaN/non-numeric skipping, and a combined ground/hallucinate scenario); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. (`generateSpxCommentary` itself has no direct test ‚Äî same as its sibling `spx-play-claude.ts` ‚Äî Anthropic API calls with no existing mocking harness in this file's test suite; the new shared logic it depends on is directly tested instead.)

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `fmtPremium` had 8 hand-copied siblings rendering different strings for the same dollar figure (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/api.ts`'s `fmtPremium` (sign-outside-glyph, B/M/K ladder, `<10K` keeps 1 decimal, `>=10K` whole-K) was independently reimplemented in 8 places, each with subtle divergences: `polygon-options-gex.ts:1472` (`fmtShiftMoney`, no finite guard, always-1-decimal K), `spx-commentary.ts:23/37` (`fmtPrem`/`fmtGexUsd` ‚Äî `fmtPrem` had **no sign extraction at all**, so negatives rendered `"$-1.2M"` instead of `"-$1.2M"`, plus no B tier), `gex-positioning.ts:120` (`fmtMoney`, always-1-decimal K, `"n/a"` instead of `"‚Äî"`), `gex-heatmap-display.ts:16` (`fmtHeatmapMoney`, no finite guard ‚Äî a NaN input rendered literal `"$NaN"` on the GEX heatmap cells ‚Äî plus an extra `abs<1‚Üí"$0.0K"` branch), `nighthawk/format.ts:150` (`fmtPrem`, no B tier, `Math.round` K with no decimal), `nighthawk/grounding.ts:458` (`humanDollars`, no `$` prefix, no sign, no B tier), `largo/flow-strike-stacks.ts:155` (`fmtFlowPremShort`, unique 3-tier K logic, no B tier), `zerodte/intel.ts:19` (`money`, no sign extraction ‚Äî same `"$-1.2M"` bug as `spx-commentary.ts` ‚Äî and `.toFixed(2)` cents below $1K instead of whole dollars). Same dollar figure rendered as a different string depending which surface displayed it ‚Äî the exact cross-surface consistency bug class the audit's own BIE-as-auditor proposal calls out by name.

**Fix:** extracted `fmtPremium` into a new dependency-free `src/lib/fmt-money.ts` (no framework imports, safe for client and server), re-exported it from `api.ts` for back-compat (`export { fmtPremium } from "@/lib/fmt-money"` ‚Äî 30+ existing `.tsx` consumers unchanged), then deleted all 8 local reimplementations and routed their call sites through the canonical formatter. Two files needed the same import-plus-export pattern used in the `et-date.ts` consolidation (a bare re-export doesn't create a local binding): `gex-heatmap-display.ts`'s `fmtHeatmapMoney` (used internally by `fmtHeatmapMoneySigned` in the same file) and `largo/flow-strike-stacks.ts`'s `fmtFlowPremShort` (used internally by `formatFlowStrikeStackLine`) both now do `import { fmtPremium as <name> } from "@/lib/fmt-money"; export { <name> };` so external consumers (`GexHeatmap.tsx`/`SpxGexMatrixHeatmap.tsx`, `StrikeStackDetector.tsx`) needed zero changes. `nighthawk/grounding.ts`'s `humanDollars` had no `$` prefix (callers prepended it manually) ‚Äî updated its one call site to stop double-prefixing now that `fmtPremium` includes the `$`.

**Blast radius (real display-string changes, not just internal refactor):** consolidating onto one K-branch rule (`<$10K` keeps 1 decimal, `>=$10K` rounds to whole K) changes the rendered string in several surfaces that previously used unconditional 1-decimal K ‚Äî most visibly the GEX heatmap cells (`GexHeatmap.tsx`, `SpxGexMatrixHeatmap.tsx` via `fmtHeatmapMoneySigned`), where e.g. `$22.1K` now renders `$22K`. This is the intended fix, not a regression: it's the same "different string for the same number" bug the audit flagged, now resolved in the canonical formatter's favor since that's the version 30+ other desk components already render. Two real sign-placement bugs are fixed for free: `spx-commentary.ts`'s `fmtPrem` and `zerodte/intel.ts`'s `money` both put the negative sign *inside* the `$` (`"$-1.2M"`); the canonical formatter always extracts it first (`"-$1.2M"`). Updated one existing test (`gex-heatmap-display.test.ts`) whose assertion hardcoded the old always-1-decimal-K string.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean across all 9 touched files; full suite `956/956` passing (6 new, covering the canonical formatter's sign/tier/finite-guard behavior); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Extracted the numeric-grounding fabrication guard into a shared module (audit finding, prerequisite)
**Where:** `src/app/api/market/gex-heatmap/explain/route.ts`'s `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded()` was the ONLY LLM-narrative surface in the codebase with a post-generation fabrication check (extract every number that reads like a price level from the model's prose, confirm it matches a known-good value, fall back to a deterministic line otherwise). The audit found 6 other LLM call sites shipping prose with zero such guard: `spx-play-claude.ts`, `spx-commentary.ts`, `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts`, `flow-brief/route.ts`, `nights-watch/position-narrative.ts`, `nighthawk/play-critic.ts`. The audit's fix for each of those explicitly calls for reusing "the shared numeric guard" / "that route's `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded` guard" ‚Äî which didn't exist as a shared, importable primitive before this PR.

**Fix:** extracted the domain-agnostic core of `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded` (the number-extraction regex, the %/money/small-int/out-of-band filters, the tolerance-scaled match against a caller-supplied `known: number[]` array) into a new `checkNumbersGrounded(text, known)` in `src/lib/grounding-guard.ts`, returning `{ grounded, ungroundedValue }` so callers can log the specific offending number. `gex-heatmap/explain/route.ts` keeps its heatmap-specific `knownPriceLevels()` (strikes/spot/max_pain/gex-vex-dex-charm levels/dark-pool overlays) local ‚Äî that part is genuinely domain-specific ‚Äî and `narrativeLevelsAreGrounded` is now a 9-line wrapper that calls `knownPriceLevels()` then `checkNumbersGrounded()`, preserving byte-identical behavior (same regex, same tolerance formula, same warn-and-fallback contract).

**Blast radius:** none yet ‚Äî this PR is purely the extraction (verified behavior-preserving on the one existing consumer). Tasks to apply this guard to the 6 other LLM surfaces follow as separate PRs per the standing one-issue-per-PR policy, since each surface needs its own "known good numbers" source wired up (chain/dossier data, position Greeks, dossier flow figures, etc.) and its own fallback behavior per the audit's per-file fix instructions.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `960/960` passing (10 new for `grounding-guard.ts`, covering percentages/money/small-ints/out-of-band filtering, tolerance-scaled matching, and the ungrounded-value diagnostic); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî 0DTE Command board's freshness badge was a hardcoded `"live"` literal (launch blocker)
**Where:** `src/components/zerodte/ZeroDteBoard.tsx:198` passed `status="live"` into `FreshnessChip` as a literal, never derived from any success/failure signal, and `data.as_of` (`route.ts:99`) was just response-build time ‚Äî independent of whether the underlying scan actually produced data. `scanZeroDteBoard()`'s flow fetch (`scan.ts:116`, `fetchRecentFlows({...}).catch(() => [])`) silently degraded to zero setups on any UW/DB failure, and the route still returned `available:true`. Result: a silently-failed upstream scan rendered as a calm, current, green-badged empty board ‚Äî indistinguishable from a genuinely quiet tape, and the board's own reassuring empty-state copy ("No A-tier play right now ‚Äî and that's the discipline...") made this worse, not better.

**Fix:** threaded a real `upstream_ok` boolean from the tape-fetch `.catch()` (now sets `upstreamOk = false` instead of silently swallowing) through `ZeroDteScanResult` ‚Üí `buildBoardPayload` ‚Üí the API response. Added `resolveZeroDteFreshness(upstreamOk, asOfMs, nowMs, staleAfterMs=60_000)` ‚Äî a pure function replacing the hardcoded literal: `upstream_ok===false` ‚Üí `"offline"`; response older than 60s (6x the board's 10s active-session poll interval) ‚Üí `"stale"`; otherwise `"live"`. Mirrors the existing `SpxSniperHeader.tsx`'s `resolveFreshness()` age-derived pattern, generalized with the upstream-failure signal this board didn't previously have.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `945/945` passing (5 new); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Six duplicate `todayEtYmd`-style ET-date implementations, one already byte-drifted (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** the ET session-calendar-date formula (`new Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-CA", { timeZone: "America/New_York" }).format(...)`) was hand-copied into 6 separate local functions instead of importing the canonical `todayEt()` in `src/lib/et-date.ts` (itself the prior consolidation of ~7 other copies ‚Äî this batch was the stragglers that predated or were added alongside that consolidation): `src/lib/providers/spx-session.ts` (exported `todayEtYmd`), `src/lib/et-market-hours.ts` (local, unexported, took a `now` param), `src/lib/providers/macro-events.ts` (local, unexported, 4 call sites), `src/lib/spx-play-session-guards.ts` (local, unexported, gates `EARLY_CLOSE_DATES` lookup), `src/lib/session-cache.ts` (exported `todayEtYmdClient`, consumed externally by `useSpxPlay.ts` and `useSpxDayPerformance.ts`), and `src/lib/correctness/heatmap-verifier.ts` + `src/lib/correctness/desk-verifier.ts` (both a byte-identical local `todayEtYmdLocal()`, no `now` param). Six separate copies of a date-boundary formula is itself a latent-bug generator ‚Äî the exact failure mode `et-date.ts`'s own header comment documents from the last time this happened (a copy silently drifting, e.g. by locale/format options), and one of these bare-`CURRENT_DATE` classes of bug had already shipped and been fixed earlier this audit (`db.ts:3873`, PR #402).

**Fix:** replaced all 7 duplicate function bodies with imports of the canonical `todayEt()` (or `import { todayEt as <localName> }` where the file's exported name differs, to keep every external call site source-compatible). Two required care beyond a straight swap: (1) `session-cache.ts` externally exports `todayEtYmdClient` while also using it internally at 3 call sites in the same file ‚Äî a bare `export { todayEt as todayEtYmdClient } from "@/lib/et-date"` re-export doesn't create a local binding, so it needed both `import { todayEt as todayEtYmdClient } from "@/lib/et-date"` (for internal use) *and* `export { todayEt as todayEtYmdClient } from "@/lib/et-date"` (for the external contract) ‚Äî confirmed via `tsc` catching the internal-binding gap on the first attempt; (2) `et-market-hours.ts`'s local version took an explicit `now: Date` parameter (the module's own `isEtCashRth(now)` threads a caller-supplied clock) ‚Äî confirmed `todayEt(now)` accepts the same optional param with an identical `new Date()` default, so this was a like-for-like swap, not a behavior change.

**Blast radius:** no behavior change anywhere ‚Äî `et-date.ts`'s header comment already asserts byte-identical output to the copies it replaces (same `en-CA` locale, same timeZone, no year/month/day option fields), verified by inspection at every one of the 7 sites before deleting. Zero call-site signature changes; the two exported aliases (`todayEtYmd`, `todayEtYmdClient`) are preserved so `useSpxPlay.ts`/`useSpxDayPerformance.ts`/every other external consumer needed no changes.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean across all 7 files; full suite `940/940` passing; `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `NetPremiumLeaderboard` conflated loading with a genuinely quiet tape (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/components/desk/NetPremiumLeaderboard.tsx` had no `loading` prop; the render gate `rows.length === 0 ? <skeletons> : <rows>` couldn't distinguish "awaiting first data" from "data loaded, zero qualifying rows," so a genuinely quiet period looked identical to a stuck/broken panel indefinitely. `FlowFeed.tsx` already computes a `loading` state (line 109, already threaded into `FlowAlertStream`) but wasn't passing it here.

**Fix:** added an optional `loading` prop (default `false`, backward-compatible), threaded `FlowFeed`'s existing state through at the one call site, gated the skeleton on `loading === true`, and added a real empty-state message ("No net-premium leaders yet ‚Äî quiet tape.") for `loading === false && rows.length === 0` ‚Äî mirroring the sibling `StrikeStackDetector`'s existing steady-state-message pattern for the identical condition.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `FlowAlertStream`'s DTE fallback undercounted across DST (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/components/desk/FlowAlertStream.tsx` ‚Äî `calcDte()` (the fallback used whenever the API omits `flow.dte`) parsed both today and expiry via local-time `new Date(...)` (no `Z` suffix) and returned `Math.floor(...)`, diverging from the canonical UTC-anchored, `Math.round`-based `daysToExpiry()` in `nights-watch/valuation.ts`. A local-midnight span crossing one DST transition is off by exactly 1 hour from a multiple of a day, which `Math.floor` turns into a 1-day undercount.

**Fix:** deleted `calcDte()` entirely, imported and used the canonical `daysToExpiry` from `@/lib/nights-watch/valuation` instead. Confirmed client-safe: both `et-date.ts` (which `daysToExpiry` calls via `todayEt`) and `valuation.ts` itself are explicitly documented as importable from client modules (no `"server-only"`, no Node-only deps ‚Äî their only non-type imports are other pure functions), and the production build output shows no bundle-size regression or error.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `935/935` passing; `npm run build` clean (client bundle unaffected); `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Internal vs. public win-rate rounding could disagree (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/lib/track-record-page.ts`'s `spxFromStats()` rounded win-rate to 1 decimal (`Math.round(x*1000)/10`); `src/lib/track-record-public.ts`'s `pct()` independently rounded the same fraction to an integer (`Math.round(x*100)`) ‚Äî two hand-written formulas over the same input that can double-round-diverge on some fractions (e.g. `0.6245` rounds to `62.5` at 1dp, but a *separately*-computed integer formula landing on `62` instead of the consistent `63` that re-rounding `62.5` itself gives is a real, silent split-brain a member could notice by comparing `/track-record` to the public share card). `pageSpxMatchesPublic()` (the dedicated consistency verifier) only ever compared total/wins/losses, never the win-rate field itself.

**Fix:** extracted `formatPercent(fraction, dp)` in `track-record-public.ts` as the single shared rounding formula, used at both call sites (`dp=1` internal, `dp=0` public) plus Night Hawk's own win-rate calc in the same file (same formula, same cleanup). Extended `pageSpxMatchesPublic()` to assert the two sides agree when re-rounded to the same precision via that same function ‚Äî this is what actually catches a future re-divergence, not just checking the numbers look similar.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite `935/935` passing (4 new); `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

**Where:** `src/app/api/account/positions/[id]/detail/route.ts` ‚Äî `net_gex` values pulled directly from raw GEX `strike_totals` (via `buildPositionDetail`'s `gexWallsFromHeatmapSpot`) could reach the wire with float noise, the one route skipping the `roundFloats()` convention every sibling GEX-consuming route applies. Currently masked by the frontend's `.toFixed()`.

**Fix:** wrapped the response body in `roundFloats({ ...detail, narrative })`. `roundFloats` only touches numeric leaves in the tree (strings, including the AI `narrative` field, pass through untouched), so this is purely additive.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `/api/ready` leaked raw DB driver error text publicly (audit finding, medium/security)

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `/api/ready` never checked Redis (audit finding, medium)
**Where:** `src/app/api/ready/route.ts` ‚Äî the Railway-wired healthcheck only called `pingDatabaseConnectivity()`. `probeRedisHealth()` already existed but its only call site was the admin-only `/api/admin/bie-report` route, so a replica with dead Redis was marked fully healthy while rate limits, WS leader locks, and caches silently failed open with no visible signal.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî `fetchNighthawkOutcomeAnalytics` regressed the bare-`CURRENT_DATE` bug a second time

Surfaced by tonight's CEO/CTO production audit (`docs/audit/CEO-CTO-AUDIT-20260704.md`, launch-blocker-adjacent finding #7), which flagged this as a **regression of the identical bug class already found and fixed once in `confluence-outcomes.ts`'s 60-day window** ‚Äî the fix was never mirrored here.

**Fix:** swapped `CURRENT_DATE` for the established `(NOW() AT TIME ZONE 'America/New_York')::date` pattern already used elsewhere in the same file (`db.ts:1329`) and in `confluence-outcomes.ts:133`. Added a source-text regression test (`db.test.ts`) asserting the query text can't silently revert to bare `CURRENT_DATE` a third time ‚Äî the function isn't otherwise unit-testable without a live Postgres connection.

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî All 4 WS leader-lock managers failed OPEN unconditionally on Redis loss, regardless of replica count (audit finding, high)
**Where:** `src/lib/ws/uw-socket.ts` (`tryAcquireUwLead`), `polygon-socket.ts` (`tryAcquireIndicesLead`), `options-socket.ts` (`tryAcquireOptionsLead`), and `stocks-socket.ts` (`tryAcquireStocksLead`) each hold a Redis SETNX lock so only ONE replica opens its upstream WebSocket ‚Äî Massive/UW allow at most one live connection per API key, and the 2nd‚ÄìNth replica gets rejected (code 1008) and churns reconnects forever. All four returned `true` ("allow the WS ‚Äî single-replica safe / fail-open") unconditionally whenever `getUwCacheRedis()` returned null OR the lock read threw, with a comment explicitly (and only conditionally correctly) calling this "single-replica safe." Production runs 5 replicas (`docs/PGBOUNCER-SETUP.md`). A Redis outage ‚Äî however brief ‚Äî would make every one of those 5 replicas simultaneously believe it's the leader, each opening its own WS, turning a transient Redis blip into a cluster-wide reconnect storm on all four socket types for the full outage window. `REPLICA_COUNT` already exists and is used for exactly this kind of degraded-Redis multi-replica gating in `uw-rate-limiter.ts`/`polygon-rate-limiter.ts`/`admin-health.ts`, but was absent from all four WS lock sites.

**Fix:** new shared `src/lib/ws/leader-lock-shared.ts` ‚Äî `wsLeaderShouldFailOpenWithoutRedis(replicaCount = REPLICA_COUNT)` returns `true` only when `replicaCount <= 1` (no peer to contend with, so fail-open is genuinely safe), plus a one-time ops alert (`alertWsLeaderFailClosedOnce`, re-armed by `clearWsLeaderFailClosedAlert` on the next successful lock read) mirroring `uw-rate-limiter.ts`'s existing `alertRedisDegradedOnce` pattern. All four `tryAcquire*Lead()` functions now check this before returning `true` on missing/errored Redis: single-replica keeps the old fail-open behavior unchanged; multi-replica fails CLOSED (returns `false`, so `ensure*Leadership()` treats this replica as a standby, which every one of the four sockets already handles via its existing REST/Redis-snapshot fallback path ‚Äî no new fallback logic needed).

**Fix rationale:** fail-CLOSED (not "add jitter before fail-open," the audit's alternative suggestion) was chosen because jittered fail-open still has every replica eventually try to open the socket ‚Äî it only staggers *when* the storm starts, not whether N-1 of them still get rejected and churn. Fail-closed means at most one replica is ever attempting the WS at a time (the Redis SETNX path, once it recovers), and every one of these four sockets was already built with a non-WS fallback for standbys (UW: Postgres-persisted flow_alerts + REST for tide/dark-pool; Polygon indices: `spx:pulse:snapshot` Redis read; options marks: leader's `nw:optmark:` Redis write-through; stocks/LULD: the position/play-gate code already tolerates the feed being absent) ‚Äî so failing closed costs a temporary loss of the *live push*, not a loss of data entirely, which is a better trade than a reconnect storm during the exact Redis-degraded window when the cluster is least equipped to absorb one.

**Blast radius:** exactly the 4 files named in the audit finding, each touched at exactly its one `tryAcquire*Lead()` function ‚Äî no change to leadership-refresh, release, or the reconcile-tick call sites, since `ensure*Leadership()` already correctly treats a `false` return as "not leader, stand down."

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite passing (4 new in `leader-lock-shared.test.ts` ‚Äî default REPLICA_COUNT=1 fails open, explicit multi-replica counts fail closed, replicaCount<=1 fails open, alert latch/clear don't throw regardless of whether the Discord webhook is configured). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

---

## üü¢ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Largo streamed raw model text live, before its own numeric verifier ever ran, and never surfaced which specific numbers were unverified (audit finding, launch blocker ‚Äî both halves closed)
**Where:** `src/lib/largo-terminal.ts` streamed every model token live via `onEvent` (`anthropicToolLoop` ‚Üí `providers/anthropic.ts`'s `stream.on("text", ...)`) before the Layer-4 numeric verifier (`verifyClaims`) ever ran ‚Äî a member could read (and act on) a fabricated strike/premium before any check fired. Only after the full loop resolved did the code append a trailing, vague in-text caveat ‚Äî and only when `verification.total >= 4 && verification.coverage < 0.5` (both `runLargoQuery` at line ~338 and `runLargoQueryStream` at line ~463). `verifyClaims()` already computed and returned `unverified: number[]` (the actual figures that failed to trace), but neither function ever read it ‚Äî only `.total`/`.verified`/`.coverage` ‚Äî so even when the threshold DID fire, a member only saw "N of M figures could not be traced," never which N.

**Fix, both audit-specified halves, in two commits on this branch:**
1. **Always surface `unverified`:** the full `ClaimVerification` object (`{ total, verified, unverified, coverage }`) is now always included as a structured `verification` field on every terminal result ‚Äî both `runLargoQuery`'s return object and every `LargoStreamEvent` "done" event emitted by `runLargoQueryStream` (all 4 emission sites: the BIE-router fast path and the Claude tool-loop path, in both the streaming and non-streaming functions), unconditionally, independent of the existing in-text caveat's own threshold. Threaded through the client-side SSE parser (`queryLargoStream` in `api.ts`) for a complete wire contract, without touching any `.tsx` rendering component.
2. **Buffer until verified:** `runLargoQueryStream`'s Claude tool-loop `onEvent` callback now forwards `tool_start` events live (deterministic tool names ‚Äî safe, and keeps the existing "thinking" tool-trace UI working unchanged) but drops raw `token` text deltas instead of forwarding them. `anthropicToolLoop`'s resolved return value still carries the full text regardless of which events are forwarded, so `verifyClaims()` now always runs against the complete answer *before* any of it reaches the client. The verified (and, if applicable, caveat-appended) text is then delivered as a single `token` event immediately followed by `done` ‚Äî mirroring the BIE-router fast path's own already-existing single-token-then-done pattern a few lines up in the same file, rather than inventing a new delivery shape.

**Why buffer everything instead of the audit's literal "high-stakes intents only" suggestion:** classifying which intents count as "high-stakes" is itself a judgment call with real room for a gap (a casually-phrased question can still elicit a fabricated price), and the codebase's existing intent classifier (`question-intent.ts`) has no such dimension today ‚Äî every existing category there is topical (SPX desk / play-state / flow / news / vol), not risk-tiered. Buffering universally is simpler, has no classification-gap failure mode, and costs only the time between Claude finishing generation and `verifyClaims()` returning (that function is a synchronous regex-based check ‚Äî negligible added latency on top of a synthesis step that already took as long as it took). The user-visible change is bounded: the "thinking" tool-trace indicator (already shown while tools run) now also covers the final-synthesis window that previously showed live-typed tokens ‚Äî the frontend's existing loading state already handles this gap with zero code changes, confirmed by reading `LargoTerminal.tsx`'s streaming/thinking-state logic (not modified by this fix).

**Blast radius:** `largo-terminal.ts` (`LargoStreamEvent` type, the tool-loop `onEvent` filter, and both functions' return/emit sites) and `api.ts` (`queryLargoStream`'s wire-contract types). The BIE-router fast path (already single-shot) and the non-streaming `runLargoQuery` (never streamed live to begin with ‚Äî already fully buffers before returning) are unchanged by part 2; only the Claude tool-loop path inside `runLargoQueryStream` had the live-token exposure. The API route (`api/market/largo/query/route.ts`) needed no change ‚Äî it already `NextResponse.json(result, ...)`s the whole object.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean; full suite passing, no regressions (`largo-terminal.ts` itself has no direct test ‚Äî confirmed by import: it throws "This module cannot be imported from a Client Component module" outside Next's server-component runtime, the same transitive `server-only` wall already documented for `src/lib/correctness/*` and `nighthawk/play-explainer.ts` elsewhere in this file). `npm run build` clean; `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

---

## üßÝ BIE semantic precedent search SHIPPED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî "has this setup happened before, and what happened"
**The gap:** BIE's L2 knowledge layer (embeddings + cosine search) has existed since Phase 2, but it only ever indexed prose ‚Äî docs, findings, editions. It never touched the platform's own structured trading history in `alert_audit_log`, so a genuinely new kind of question ‚Äî "find me past alerts that resemble this one, and what happened" ‚Äî was unanswerable; a member or Largo could only filter by exact ticker/date, never by resemblance.

**What shipped:**
- `mapAlertAuditTrailRow()` (`src/lib/db.ts`) ‚Äî extracted the raw-row‚Üítyped-row mapping that `fetchAlertAuditTrail` already did inline, so both it and the new `fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows()` share one tested mapper instead of duplicating the NUMERIC-string-column conversion logic.
- `fetchResolvedAlertAuditRows(days)` (`src/lib/db.ts`) ‚Äî every alert with a TERMINAL outcome (`target`/`stop`/`ambiguous`/`unfilled` ‚Äî deliberately excludes `open`/`pending`, since "what happened" needs an actual answer) from the last N days, uncapped unlike the admin-display `fetchAlertAuditTrail`'s 100-row limit.
- `describeAuditRow()` (`src/lib/bie/precedent-search.ts`) ‚Äî pure, deterministic, template-based row‚Üínatural-language description (e.g. "0DTE Command alert on NVDA, long, high conviction (score 82) ‚Äî fired because aggression spike. Outcome: target."). Never LLM-generated, so it can never fabricate a detail the row doesn't actually have.
- `ingestAlertPrecedents()` ‚Äî embeds every resolved alert from the last 60 days into `bie_knowledge` under a new `"precedent"` kind, wired into the existing nightly `ingestBieKnowledge()` cron. Idempotent via the existing hash-dedup: re-running over the same graded rows costs nothing.
- `findSimilarPrecedents(query, k)` ‚Äî cosine search scoped to `kind="precedent"` only, so results never mix with doc/finding prose. Required generalizing `searchKnowledge()` with an optional `kind` filter (backward-compatible ‚Äî existing call sites pass nothing and search the whole corpus, unchanged).
- New Largo tool `get_similar_precedents(query)` ‚Äî Claude composes a short description of the current setup, gets back the most similar past alerts + outcomes. Tool description is explicit that this is historical color for a member's question, **never** a live signal or a reason to change a gate/score ‚Äî consistent with the standing Stage 6 boundary (BIE never acts on outcome data, only reports it).

**Explicitly backend-only, per standing instruction:** no `.tsx`/UI files touched ‚Äî this ships as a Largo tool + knowledge-layer capability; the admin report's existing `knowledge.by_kind` breakdown (`fetchBieKnowledgeStats()`, already grouped by kind) will show the new `"precedent"` bucket automatically once ingestion runs, with no route change needed.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 905/905 passing (9 new: 3 for `mapAlertAuditTrailRow`'s DB-boundary conversion, 6 for `describeAuditRow`'s template correctness), `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üßÝ BIE landing banner redesign SHIPPED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî flat hub-and-row ‚Üí orbiting sphere-mesh, on explicit user request
**Ask:** user reviewed the live home page and asked for a real visual upgrade to the "Introducing BlackOut Intelligence Engine" banner ‚Äî the connections between BIE and the six instruments "looked not so great," suggested something sphere-like with connected dots and continuous flow, better live animation, and an explicit standing instruction to never name BlackOut's own LLM/model in this copy (consistent with the existing honest-realism stance in `docs/bie/ARCHITECTURE.md`: Claude is the general-reasoning fallback, not a proprietary model BlackOut trained).

**What changed (`src/components/landing/BieBrainBanner.tsx`, `bie-brain-geometry.ts`):**
- BIE's core moved from "perched above a row of 6 nodes" to dead-center, with the six instruments arranged on an **ellipse** (not a true circle) around it ‚Äî the rx‚âÝry asymmetry alone fakes a disc viewed at an angle, a tilted "sphere/globe" look, using plain 2D math. Considered a CSS 3D `rotateX` tilt instead; rejected because it leaves the layout box reserving full untilted space while only the paint gets foreshortened, leaving a blank gap ‚Äî the ellipse approach has no such mismatch.
- Connections went from a plain hub-and-spoke + adjacent-only mesh to three wire categories: straight core‚Üínode **spokes**, curved **ring** arcs between neighbors, and long **cross** diagonals (node *i* to *i*+2) that for 6 evenly-spaced nodes trace two overlapping triangles ‚Äî a hexagram, the densest-reading mesh for the least clutter.
- Added a 26-point **ambient dust field** (golden-angle spiral fill of the disc ‚Äî deterministic, no RNG) so the diagram reads as a dense sphere of points rather than 6 isolated dots on empty space.
- The whole node+wire ring and the dust field now **continuously rotate** (opposite directions, different speeds ‚Äî 70s/100s per revolution) around the fixed core via SVG-native `rotate()` on their own `<g>`, gated to start only once scrolled into view (`.is-drawn`). Traveling pulse dots (existing SMIL `animateMotion`/`mpath` technique, now applied to all 18 wires instead of 11) give the literal "continuous flow" the ask asked for.
- No new dependencies (no WebGL/three.js) ‚Äî everything is plain SVG + CSS, consistent with the rest of this codebase's landing-page architecture.

**Verified live**, not just built: ran the actual dev server + Playwright (Chromium is pre-installed in this sandbox at `/opt/pw-browsers/chromium`, reachable via the globally-installed `playwright` package even though it isn't a local `node_modules` dependency here) and screenshotted the rendered banner ‚Äî confirmed the sphere/mesh layout renders correctly, the ring visibly rotates over a few seconds, a traveling pulse is caught mid-flight, mobile width (390px) stays legible, and `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` renders a fully-static, fully-drawn network with zero animation, matching the existing accessibility contract.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 892/892 passing (4 new geometry tests replacing 4 stale ones for the removed circle/mesh helpers), `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor`/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green. Grepped the new copy for "LLM"/"model" ‚Äî no occurrence, per the standing instruction.

## üî¥ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî Public landing page leaked internal infra (Railway, cron, CPU/memory/env-vars) in the BIE banner copy; vendor guard had a gap
**Root cause:** `src/components/landing/BieBrainBanner.tsx`'s rotating subtitle under the "Introducing BlackOut Intelligence Engine" banner ‚Äî a public, unauthenticated marketing surface on the home page ‚Äî included two lines naming internal infrastructure by name: `"cron & worker health ‚Äî 20+ jobs tracked, schedule-aware"` and `"Railway deploy, CPU, memory, and env-vars ‚Äî watched live"`. This is a vendor/stack-leak issue the repo already has a dedicated guard for (`npm run lint:vendor` / `scripts/check-vendor-surfaces.mjs`, which explicitly scans `src/components/landing`), but the guard's `VENDORS` regex never included `Railway` ‚Äî so a real, member-visible leak sat on the home page passing CI the whole time. "cron"/"CPU"/"env-vars" aren't vendor names so the regex-based guard was never going to catch those regardless; those are copy-quality issues, not something a name-matching guard can generically enforce.

**Fix:**
1. Rewrote both `READOUT_LINES` entries in `BieBrainBanner.tsx` to be stack-free and, per explicit request, catchier ‚Äî `"the desk never sleeps ‚Äî every system checked, every minute of the day"` and `"uptime, speed, stability ‚Äî watched live, so you never have to ask"` ‚Äî matching the existing lines' tone (`"one audit trail for every 0DTE and Night Hawk alert"`, `"the model never invents a number ‚Äî every claim is checked"`) instead of naming internal implementation.
2. Added `Railway|Voyage|Vercel` to `check-vendor-surfaces.mjs`'s `VENDORS` regex so this specific class of leak (a real vendor name, not generic ops jargon) can't silently reappear and pass CI again.
3. Added a one-line comment above `READOUT_LINES` pointing future editors at the guard, since this is a marketing surface a copy-only edit could easily reintroduce the leak into.

**Blast radius:** grepped `src/components/landing` and `src/app/(site)` for the same vendor/infra terms ‚Äî this banner was the only hit; no other member-facing surface names Railway, cron, or infra internals.

**Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 888/888 passing, `npm run build` clean, `lint:brand`/`lint:vendor` (now genuinely exercising the fix)/`verify-api-auth-guards.mjs` all green.

## üî¥ FIXED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî 8-agent review of the whole BIE ecosystem line (PRs #366‚Äì#378) found 3 real correctness bugs + 5 quality issues, all fixed
**Status:** FIXED (`fix/bie-ecosystem-review-findings`). After 13 PRs shipped in one thread, paused feature work to run a structured review (10 independent finder angles + verification + gap sweep) over the full cumulative diff (`0247146~1..60e96f9`) before anything else landed on top of it. Findings below, most severe first.

**üî¥ P1 ‚Äî `avg_move_pct` silently always `null` in production, despite real data existing.** `src/lib/bie/confluence-outcomes.ts`'s query selected `z.move_pct` (a Postgres `NUMERIC` column) straight into a field typed `number | null` with no `Number()` conversion ‚Äî node-pg returns `NUMERIC` as a **string**. `bucketConfluenceRows`'s `moves.reduce((a, b) => a + b, 0)` then does silent **string concatenation** (`0 + "1.20" + "-0.50"` ‚Üí `"01.20-0.50"`), which coerces to `NaN` on division and serializes to `null` ‚Äî indistinguishable from "no data." Independently confirmed by two separate review agents. The bucket-level unit tests never caught this because they hand-construct `ConfluenceRow` objects with real JS numbers, bypassing the exact DB boundary where the bug lived. **Fix:** extracted the raw-row‚Üí`ConfluenceRow` mapping into a new pure, exported, unit-tested function (`mapConfluenceRows`, 3 new tests including a literal reproduction of the string-concat failure), matching this session's established split-pure-logic-for-testability pattern.

**üüÝ P2 ‚Äî Same query's 60-day window used `CURRENT_DATE` (server/session timezone) instead of the codebase's established ET-date convention.** Every other ET-sensitive date-window query in `db.ts` explicitly uses `(NOW() AT TIME ZONE 'America/New_York')::date` (with a comment at `db.ts:1327` warning against bare `CURRENT_DATE`) ‚Äî this one didn't. Between ~8pm‚Äìmidnight ET, `CURRENT_DATE` is already the next UTC day, shifting the 60-day cutoff forward and dropping the oldest ET session a day early ‚Äî enough to flip `insufficient_sample` right at the `MIN_SAMPLE = 10` boundary depending purely on what time the report happens to run. **Fix:** switched to the standard `(NOW() AT TIME ZONE 'America/New_York')::date` expression.

**üüÝ P2 ‚Äî HELIX's new `alert_audit_log` write (PR #370) could duplicate on a transient-DB-failure + WS/REST double-delivery.** The write was gated on `shouldPublish`, which is also `true` when the `flow_alerts` insert **threw** (`insertFailed`, an intentionally permissive fallback so the live tape/Discord still fire even when dedup is uncertain). `insertAlertAuditLog` has no uniqueness constraint of its own. If a transient Postgres blip hit both the WS and REST-backup delivery of the same whale print, both branches could independently write an `alert_audit_log` row for the identical print ‚Äî violating the exact one-row-per-alert invariant `fetchDuplicateAlertGroups` (Stage 2) exists to police. **Fix:** gated on `inserted` specifically (only `true` after a confirmed `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING ... RETURNING` genuinely creates a new row) instead of `shouldPublish` ‚Äî matches the same certainty guarantee 0DTE/Night Hawk's audit-log writes already rely on.

**üü° P3 ‚Äî HELIX's `direction` ("bullish"/"bearish"/"unknown") wrote a THIRD raw vocabulary into a column already split between 0DTE's lowercase "long"/"short" and Night Hawk's uppercase "LONG"/"SHORT".** Not just a display inconsistency ‚Äî any future direction-equality read across all three `alert_audit_log` producers (the exact pattern `confluence-outcomes.ts` just established for 0DTE vs. Night Hawk) would silently mis-bucket every HELIX row. **Fix:** new pure `normalizeHelixDirection()` maps bullish‚Üílong, bearish‚Üíshort, unknown‚Üínull (never guessed) ‚Äî the shared column now has two vocabularies, not three. 3 new tests.

**üü° P3 ‚Äî `fetchHotTickers`'s "over-fetch 3x then filter" heuristic could still silently return fewer than `limit` results.** On a day where SPY/QQQ/VIX/leveraged-ETP premium dominates, more than 16 of the top 24 fetched rows (3√ó the default `limit=8`) can be excluded names ‚Äî the function would return fewer than 8 tickers with zero signal that anything was truncated. **Fix:** moved the exclusion into the SQL `WHERE` clause (`NOT (ticker = ANY($1::text[]))`) so filtering happens before `LIMIT`, not after ‚Äî eliminates the under-fill risk by construction instead of padding the multiplier further. `filterHotTickers` stays as a redundant second-pass safety net (and keeps its own unit tests).

**üü° P3 ‚Äî `get_ecosystem_context`'s tool description and doc comment overclaimed `nighthawk_recent` covers "published or rejected" plays.** `nighthawk_play_outcomes` never receives a rejected play by design (`buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow`'s own doc comment: "a rejected play is never written to that table") ‚Äî a rejection is only visible via `recent_audit_entries`' `nighthawk_rejected` alert_type. Left uncorrected, a member could ask Largo "did Night Hawk reject NVDA" and get a false "no rejection on record" from a stale/absent `nighthawk_recent` instead of being pointed at the field that actually has the answer. **Fix:** corrected both the Largo tool description and the `fetchEcosystemContext` doc comment to say PUBLISHED only, with an explicit pointer to `recent_audit_entries`.

**üü° P3 ‚Äî `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` reimplemented `fmtPremium` instead of importing the canonical one.** The local copy lacked the canonical `src/lib/api.ts` version's bug fixes: NaN/Infinity guard, correct negative-sign placement (`-$1.2M` not `$-1.2M`), and a billions-before-millions branch order. **Fix:** deleted the local copy, imported the canonical `fmtPremium` from `@/lib/api`.

**üü° P4 ‚Äî `NIGHTHAWK_OUTCOME_LABEL` (0DTE board's Night Hawk echo) omitted `"unfilled"`**, a real, actively-used `nighthawk_play_outcomes.outcome` value (a play that gapped away from its entry band before it could fill). Fell through to the raw `?? echo.outcome` fallback instead of a normalized label. **Fix:** added `unfilled: "never filled"`.

**Noted, not fixed tonight (lower priority, tracked here rather than silently dropped):**
- Pre-existing root cause, not introduced by this diff: `flow_alerts` rows with `created_at IS NULL` (UW didn't supply a real timestamp) are invisible to both `recent_flow` and `hot_tickers`'s windowed queries, since `WHERE created_at >= ...` evaluates false for `NULL`. Undercounts live flow with no error surfaced. Fixing this means changing `flow-persist.ts`'s timestamp-fallback behavior itself, out of scope for a review-findings PR.
- Altitude suggestion: the `route === "whale"` string match (`isHelixAuditWorthy`) and the direction-casing fix (now fixed in 2 places, `confluence-outcomes.ts` and `ZeroDteBoard.tsx`) are both correct but ad hoc per-comparison-site fixes rather than a shared `FlowRoute` literal type / `normalizeDirection()` helper. Reasonable follow-up if a third comparison site is ever added; not urgent since both current fixes are tested and correct today.
- Duplicate ticker-list normalize+dedup one-liner (`upperTickers = [...new Set(tickers.map(...))]`) exists in 5+ places across the codebase (`ecosystem-context.ts`, `db.ts` √ó3, `ws/stocks-socket.ts`, `nights-watch/position-context.ts`) with no shared helper ‚Äî pre-existing pattern this PR added one more instance of, not a new problem.

**Verification:** 888/888 tests pass (882 + 6 new: 3 in `confluence-outcomes.test.ts` for `mapConfluenceRows`, 3 in `flow-persist.test.ts` for `normalizeHelixDirection`), `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

## üßÝ BIE ecosystem-context: recent_anomalies SHIPPED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî a third real consumer of flow_anomalies
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-ecosystem-anomalies`). `flow_anomalies` (written every 30min by the `market-regime-detector` cron, which already dedups by `(anomaly_type, ticker)` within a 15-minute window at write time) already had two consumers before this: Night Hawk's own `platform-intel-snapshot.ts` and the member-facing `/api/market/anomalies` feed. `fetchEcosystemContext` had zero visibility into it ‚Äî this adds the last 24h of pattern-detected anomalies (`CONCENTRATION`, `COORDINATED_SWEEP`, `PREMIUM_SPIKE`, `PUT_SURGE`) for the ticker as `recent_anomalies`.

**Why this is distinct from `recent_flow` (previous entries), not redundant:** `recent_flow` is a raw premium aggregate from `flow_alerts` ‚Äî count and call/put totals, no pattern judgment. `flow_anomalies` is the regime detector's own classification of a *pattern* in that flow (a coordinated sweep vs. a premium spike vs. simple concentration) ‚Äî a different kind of signal computed by a different write-path, not a re-derivation of the same numbers.

**Implementation:** one more query added to the existing `Promise.all` in `fetchEcosystemContext`, exact field names matched to the live `/api/market/anomalies` route (`anomaly_type`, `detected_at`, `detail`, `severity`, `direction`) rather than guessed. Updated the `get_ecosystem_context` Largo tool description to mention the new field.

**Verification:** 882/882 tests pass (no new tests ‚Äî a single additional aggregate query with no branching logic, same no-unit-test precedent as `recent_flow`), `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

## üßÝ BIE ecosystem: hot-tickers leaderboard SHIPPED 2026-07-04 ‚Äî the "what's hot right now" complement to recent_flow
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-hot-tickers`). `recent_flow` (previous entry) answers "how much flow has THIS ticker seen" for a name the caller already picked. This adds the other half: "which tickers are seeing the most flow, period" ‚Äî a leaderboard, not a per-ticker lookup.

**What it does:** `fetchHotTickers()` (`src/lib/bie/hot-tickers.ts`) aggregates `flow_alerts` by ticker over a 6h window (print count + total premium), same source table as `recent_flow`, different question. Wired into `/api/admin/bie-report` (`hot_tickers`) and a new "Hot tickers" panel in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx`.

**Why index/ETF/leveraged names are excluded:** SPY/QQQ/leveraged ETPs carry enormous baseline volume every single day ‚Äî an unfiltered leaderboard would show the same 2-3 names permanently and never surface genuinely unusual single-name attention, which is the entire point of a "what's hot" view. Reused `INDEX_SET`/`LEVERAGED_ETP_SET` from `src/lib/nighthawk/constants.ts` rather than inventing a new exclusion list ‚Äî same classification Night Hawk's own candidate filter already relies on.

**Verification:** `filterHotTickers` (the pure exclusion logic) unit tested in isolation (5 tests). 882/882 tests pass, `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

## üß≠ DECISION 2026-07-04 ‚Äî evaluated the "unified BIE ticker dossier" idea, built a smaller thing instead
**Original idea:** extend `fetchEcosystemContext` into a full admin/support "ask about any ticker" dossier by also folding in `error_events` and `admin_incidents`, on top of the existing 0DTE/Night Hawk/audit-log fields.

**Why it didn't ship as scoped:** checked both tables' actual schemas before building anything. `error_events` has no ticker column ‚Äî only a free-form `meta_json` JSONB, and grepping every `captureError()` call site confirmed **none of them pass a ticker into meta**, so a ticker filter on this table would always return empty. `admin_incidents` has no ticker linkage at all ‚Äî it's system-component incidents (cron failures, deploy issues), not ticker-scoped by nature. Building the dossier as originally conceived would have shipped a feature that mostly returns nulls for 2 of its 3 new fields ‚Äî exactly the "invented ground truth" this doc has been correcting all session, just in a new spot.

**What shipped instead:** `fetchEcosystemContext` gained a fourth real field, `recent_flow` ‚Äî a same-day HELIX flow summary (print count + call/put premium totals, 6h window) read directly from `flow_alerts`, not just the $1M+ whale tier that reaches `alert_audit_log`. This is genuinely non-empty today (unlike a ticker-dossier's error/incident fields) and closes a real gap: until now `fetchEcosystemContext` had zero visibility into ordinary (sub-whale) options flow at all. Reported as `call_premium` / `put_premium` / `unknown_premium` ‚Äî never collapsed into a single bullish/bearish label, per `flow_alerts`' own "TRUTH MANDATE" precedent (`parseUwFlowAlert`, `unusual-whales.ts`) against fabricating a directional default for an unparseable option side.

**Verification:** 877/877 tests pass (no new tests needed ‚Äî `recent_flow` is a single aggregate query with no branching logic to unit-test in isolation, same precedent as the rest of `fetchEcosystemContext`), `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

---

## üßÝ BIE Stage 4 gap closed SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî HELIX whale prints now write to alert_audit_log
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-helix-whale-audit-writepath`). Found while extending the ecosystem work above: `alert_audit_log`'s "unified per-alert audit trail" (Stage 4, marked SHIPPED) only ever covered 0DTE Command + Night Hawk (published/rejected) ‚Äî confirmed by grepping every `insertAlertAuditLog` call site, all in `zerodte/scan.ts` and `nighthawk/play-outcomes.ts`. HELIX (`flow-persist.ts`), the platform's highest-volume alert source, never wrote to it at all. That made it invisible to everything built on top of the audit trail this session: `fetchEcosystemContext`'s `recent_audit_entries`, Largo's `get_ecosystem_context` tool, and the duplicate-alert detector.

**Why not log the full flow tape:** HELIX's base materiality floor (`MIN_PREMIUM`, $200k default) fires far more often per day than 0DTE (a handful of flags) or Night Hawk (a handful of picks/night) ‚Äî writing every qualifying print would swamp a table sized around low-frequency sources with a high-frequency one. Used the tier that already exists for this exact reason: `route === "whale"` (premium ‚â• $1M, `unusual-whales.ts`), the same bar HELIX already uses for its own Discord üêã distinction ‚Äî no new threshold invented, reused the one the codebase already treats as "notable."

**Implementation:** `isHelixAuditWorthy()` + `buildHelixAuditRow()` (`src/lib/flow-persist.ts`) are pure, unit-tested in isolation. Wired into the existing `shouldPublish` block in `persistAndPublishFlowAlert()` ‚Äî same gate that already prevents duplicate Discord posts from a WS+REST double-delivery, so this reuses the existing dedup instead of adding a new one. Fire-and-forget (`void ... .catch()`), matching the existing `notifyDiscord` pattern ‚Äî an audit-log write failure must never block the live flow tape.

**Free upgrade to existing consumers:** because every consumer of `alert_audit_log` already reads it generically by `alert_type`, whale prints now automatically show up in Largo's ecosystem-context answers and the admin Audit Trail panel with zero further code changes ‚Äî the actual point of building this on a shared table instead of a bespoke per-consumer join.

**Verification:** `isHelixAuditWorthy`/`buildHelixAuditRow` unit tested in isolation (4 tests). 877/877 tests pass, `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 6 precursor SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî confluence-outcome measurement (does the ecosystem link mean anything?)
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-confluence-outcome-stats`). The Night Hawk echo on the 0DTE board (previous entry) is a display-only annotation ‚Äî it tells a member Night Hawk already had a take on this name, but says nothing about whether that overlap is worth anything. This closes that gap with an honest measurement, not an assumption either way.

**What it does:** `computeConfluenceOutcomeStats()` (`src/lib/bie/confluence-outcomes.ts`) joins graded `zerodte_setup_log` history (last 60 days) against each ticker's most recent PRIOR `nighthawk_play_outcomes` row (`edition_for` strictly before the 0DTE `session_date` ‚Äî same-day overlap can't exist, the scanner excludes today's live Night Hawk names by construction) and buckets every graded 0DTE flag into `agree` / `disagree` / `no_echo` by direction. Reports `n`, `hit_rate_pct`, `avg_move_pct` per bucket, and flags `insufficient_sample` under 10 rows so a small-sample hit rate is never mistaken for signal. Surfaced in `/api/admin/bie-report` (`confluence_outcomes`) and a new "Confluence outcomes" panel in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx`.

**Real bug caught before shipping, not after:** `zerodte_setup_log.direction` stores `"long"`/`"short"` (lowercase); `nighthawk_play_outcomes.direction` stores `"LONG"`/`"SHORT"` (uppercase ‚Äî see `src/lib/nighthawk/claude-edition.ts`). A literal `===` comparison between the two would have silently put every single row in `disagree`, regardless of actual agreement ‚Äî the bucketing would have looked like it worked (numbers, not an error) while being completely wrong. Caught by checking both write-paths' actual casing before writing the comparison, not by a failing test after the fact. `bucketConfluenceRows()` normalizes both sides with `.toUpperCase()` before comparing. Also fixed the same casing issue's cosmetic sibling in the Night Hawk echo note from the previous PR (was rendering `"LONG"` uppercase next to the board's otherwise-lowercase direction text).

**Deliberately read-only:** this is a measurement surface, not a feedback loop ‚Äî nothing here changes `score_max`, `conviction`, or which tickers get flagged. Whatever the numbers say (including "no correlation" or "too little data yet"), Stage 6 (closing the loop by adjusting scoring from outcomes) remains a separate, not-yet-started step per the platform charter's data-integrity-first priority.

**Verification:** `bucketConfluenceRows()` (the pure aggregator) unit tested in isolation ‚Äî 8 tests including the LONG/long casing case specifically. 874/874 tests pass, `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

---

## üßÝ BIE ecosystem-context, 2nd consumer SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî Night Hawk echo on the 0DTE board
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-nighthawk-echo-0dte-board`). `fetchEcosystemContext`'s first consumer (below) was Largo ‚Äî chat-only, a member has to think to ask. This wires the same shared-state idea into a surface every 0DTE Command viewer already sees: the board itself.

**Why it's not redundant with the existing same-day dedup:** the 0DTE scanner already excludes any ticker in *today's* live Night Hawk edition (`nighthawk_covered`, `src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts`) and tells the UI why via `covered_elsewhere`. That check only looks at the current edition, though ‚Äî a name Night Hawk picked two nights ago is fully eligible for a fresh 0DTE flag today, and until this shipped, today's ledger had zero visibility into that history. Real overlap confirmed before building this: 0DTE Command's universe is the full `flow_alerts` tape (stocks + index/ETF names, `src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts`), and Night Hawk's single-name arm explicitly excludes only indices/leveraged ETPs (`src/lib/nighthawk/constants.ts`) ‚Äî so a large-cap single name can legitimately appear in both, on different nights.

**Implementation:** `fetchNighthawkEchoForTickers()` (`src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts`) ‚Äî one batched `WHERE ticker = ANY($1)` query over the whole ledger per board build, not one `fetchEcosystemContext()` call per row (the board rebuilds every ~5-10s and a ledger can carry a couple dozen names; per-ticker round trips would scale query count with ledger size for zero benefit). Wired into `buildBoardPayload()` in `/api/market/zerodte/board/route.ts`, rendered in `ZeroDteBoard.tsx` as a small "üîó Night Hawk had this `<date>` ‚Äî `<direction>` (`<outcome>`)" line under the existing BlackOut Intel action/reason. Pure annotation ‚Äî never touches score, status, or row ordering; fails open to nothing rendered.

**Verification:** new `mapNighthawkEchoRows` pure mapper unit-tested in isolation (4 tests, same split-out-for-testability pattern as `mapDeploymentEdges`/`buildSourceApisAttribution`). 866/866 tests pass, `tsc --noEmit` + build + `lint:brand` + `lint:vendor` + API auth-guard scan all clean.

## üßÝ BIE ecosystem-context query layer, v1 SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî "what does the rest of BlackOut already know about this ticker"
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-ecosystem-context`). User's framing: BIE should work like a shared hub every instrument can query, not just a monitoring layer that reads everything after the fact. Closest real analogy is a shared-state/feature-store pattern, not network routing ‚Äî the design goal was additive, never a hard dependency: every consumer must work exactly as before if this is unreachable.

**What it does:** `fetchEcosystemContext(ticker)` (`src/lib/bie/ecosystem-context.ts`) assembles one ticker's cross-instrument snapshot from tables that already exist and are already populated by independent write-paths ‚Äî zero new data plumbing: today's 0DTE Command take (`zerodte_setup_log`), the most recent Night Hawk take (`nighthawk_play_outcomes`, published or rejected), and the last 10 `alert_audit_log` entries (the unified Stage 4 trail spanning all three write-paths). Fails open to an all-null/empty context on any error ‚Äî a lookup failure here must never block the caller's own logic, same fail-open pattern as every other BIE probe.

**First real consumer:** wired into Largo (the member-facing desk analyst) as a new tool, `get_ecosystem_context`, in the `platform` tool group alongside `get_platform_snapshot`. Deliberately the lowest-risk possible integration point ‚Äî it only affects what Largo can *cite* when answering a question, never touches scoring or alert-firing logic, so a member can now ask "what's going on with NVDA" and get an answer that spans 0DTE + Night Hawk + audit history instead of one isolated data source.

**Deliberately NOT done in this pass:** wiring this into live SCORING (e.g., Night Hawk's discovery layer treating a same-day 0DTE flag as a confirmation signal) ‚Äî that's a materially higher-risk change to logic that's been tuned carefully all session, and the "HELIX Postgres bonus" precedent showed exactly why blending cross-signals into scoring needs its own careful, direction-gated, capped design, not a quick addition. This ships the query layer and proves it with one safe consumer; scoring integration is a clearly separate future step if wanted.

**Verification:** 862/862 tests unchanged (thin DB-read wrapper, same no-unit-test precedent as `fetchAlertAuditTrail`/`getDatabasePoolStats`), `tsc --noEmit` + build + lint:brand + lint:vendor + API auth-guard scan all clean.

---

## üßÝ Stage 3 SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî Clerk auth-failure monitoring, without touching the sign-in flow
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-clerk-auth-failure-observer`). Reverses the earlier documented decision (`docs/bie/FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`, `docs/audit/FINDINGS.md` ‚Äî user chose "leave it as a permanent gap" after being warned the only known path was a full custom sign-in rewrite) ‚Äî user explicitly asked to fix it after that. Re-investigated before writing any code and found a materially safer path than the one originally presented.

**What changed vs. the original assessment:** the original research confirmed Clerk has no webhook or Backend API for a failed sign-in attempt, and concluded the only way to capture the signal was replacing the prebuilt `<SignIn>`/`<SignUp>` components with a custom `useSignIn()`-based form ‚Äî a large rewrite of a revenue-critical page, unverifiable in this sandbox (no browser). Before starting that rewrite, re-examined the problem and found a much lower-risk option: Clerk's prebuilt component already renders a visible error message on a failed attempt (styled via the `formFieldErrorText`/`alert` keys in `clerk-theme.ts` ‚Äî already live in production, so these element hooks are proven stable), and that error is regular DOM the app can observe without touching the component at all.

**Implementation:** `AuthFailureObserver.tsx` mounts as a sibling wrapper around the untouched `<SignIn>`/`<SignUp>` ‚Äî zero changes to either component, their props, or their behavior. A `MutationObserver` watches for Clerk's own error elements (matched by their stable `cl-formFieldErrorText`/`cl-alert` class markers) appearing in the DOM, reads the visible error text (never a form value, never a credential ‚Äî the observer only ever touches Clerk's own rendered error UI), and beacons it to a new public `/api/telemetry/auth-failure` endpoint (same shape as the existing `client-error` beacon: per-IP rate limited, hard body cap). Reuses the existing `error_events` sink (`captureError`, new `source: "auth_failure"`) rather than a new table. A new `countAuthFailures()` surfaces a 24h summary in `/api/admin/bie-report`, shown as a header chip in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx`.

**Risk profile, explicitly:** if Clerk ever changes its internal class naming, the observer silently stops reporting ‚Äî the auth flow itself is completely unaffected either way, since the observer never touches sign-in mechanics, only watches rendered output. This is the key property that makes it safe to ship without a live browser to test in: a bug in the observer can produce a false negative (miss a failure), never a false positive that could break login for a real member.

**Not fully live-verified:** confirming the DOM observer actually fires on a real failed attempt needs a real browser, which this sandbox doesn't have. Flagged as a follow-up ‚Äî will confirm by checking `auth_failures.total_24h` moves off zero after a genuine mistyped-password attempt occurs (or after intentionally triggering one from a browser once available).

**Verification:** 862/862 tests (9 new: `isClerkErrorClassName`/`shouldReportAuthFailure` pure-logic coverage), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean.

---

## üî¥ P0 FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî alert_audit_log's entire write-path has been silently no-op'ing since Stage 4 shipped; every prior "SHIPPED" claim in this doc and AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md was wrong
**Status:** SHIPPED (`fix/alert-audit-log-jsonb-encoding`). Found while wiring the Stage 4 `source_apis` attribution follow-up (see the entry below) ‚Äî the most severe correctness bug found this session, and it directly contradicts prior "SHIPPED" claims about Stage 4's three write-paths made across multiple earlier PRs in this doc and `docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`. Logging it prominently here per this repo's own standing policy: **never leave a false "done" claim standing once it's known to be false.**

**Root cause:** node-postgres's parameter serialization (`pg/lib/utils.js`'s `prepareValue`) converts a top-level JS **array** into a Postgres ARRAY-literal string (`{"...","..."}`), not a JSON array (`[...]`) ‚Äî confirmed empirically against the exact installed `pg` version: `prepareValue([{check:"a",...}])` produces `{"{\"check\":\"a\",...}"}`, which fails `JSON.parse` with "Expected ':' after property name." `decision_trace` (`alert_audit_log`'s `jsonb` column, always a non-empty array at both real call sites ‚Äî `buildZeroDteAuditRow` and `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow` always build a real array of check entries) hit this exact bug on **every single INSERT**, since Stage 4's write-paths first shipped. Plain objects (`source_key`, `input_snapshot`, `final_output`) were never affected ‚Äî `prepareValue`'s object branch DOES call `JSON.stringify` correctly; only a value that is a JS array at the top level hits the broken branch.

**Why nobody caught it:** both call sites fire-and-forget these inserts behind `void insertAlertAuditLog(row).catch(err => console.warn(...))` ‚Äî a deliberate design choice so an audit-log failure could never break a scan or an edition build. That same design meant the resulting Postgres error ("invalid input syntax for type json") never reached `error_events`, Sentry, or any admin-visible error surface ‚Äî it was a plain `console.warn` that only exists in Railway's raw stdout. The query surface (`fetchAlertAuditTrail`) doesn't even SELECT `decision_trace`, so no prior live-verification of the audit_trail panel (including this session's own "confirmed all six new fields present, correctly shaped" checks) would have caught this ‚Äî every prior check looked at top-level shape/counts, never at whether the underlying inserts had actually succeeded.

**Confirmed empirically, not assumed:** an authenticated GET to `/api/admin/bie-report` (same temp-Clerk-user pattern used throughout this session) returned `audit_trail: { recent: [], counts_by_type: {} }` ‚Äî **zero rows**, despite Stage 4's write-paths being marked SHIPPED across PRs today and the 0DTE scanner/Night Hawk both having run repeatedly since. A local reproduction with the exact installed `pg` package's `prepareValue` function proves the mechanism directly (see `db-audit-trail-write.test.ts`), independent of the empty-table observation (which alone could theoretically have an innocent explanation ‚Äî no fresh setups on a market holiday ‚Äî but the JSON-encoding proof does not depend on that and is conclusive on its own).

**Fix:** new `toJsonbParam()` (`db.ts`) explicitly `JSON.stringify()`s every `jsonb`-bound value before it's passed as a query parameter, with `null`/`undefined` both mapping to a real SQL `NULL`. Applied to every `jsonb` column in both `insertAlertAuditLog` and `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog` (`source_key`, `decision_trace`, `input_snapshot`, `final_output`, and the new `source_apis`) ‚Äî not just the broken one, since passing an already-correct JSON string produces byte-identical output to the driver's own object-serialization path and removes any future risk of this exact class of bug recurring if a field's shape ever changes from object to array. Added explicit `::jsonb` casts in the SQL text as defense-in-depth so Postgres unambiguously treats the parameter as JSON regardless of driver-side inference.

**Blast radius:** every 0DTE first-flag, every Night Hawk published play, and every Night Hawk rejected play since Stage 4 shipped has zero audit-trail row. Nothing else reads `alert_audit_log` for correctness-critical logic (it's a diagnostic/audit surface, not a source of truth the app depends on), so this was a visibility gap, not a data-corruption or member-facing bug ‚Äî but it means every "audit trail SHIPPED" claim this session made was false in practice, only true in code-review appearance. `docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`'s rollout section and `FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`'s Stage 4 status need a correction pass (tracked separately, not blocking this fix).

**Verification:** 853/853 tests (9 new ‚Äî `toJsonbParam` round-tripping arrays/objects/null through `JSON.parse`, `buildSourceApisAttribution`'s matching/dedup/case-insensitivity), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Full end-to-end confirmation (a real row landing in `alert_audit_log`) requires the next actual alert-firing event post-deploy ‚Äî flagged as a follow-up live-verification, not assumed from the unit-level proof alone.

---

## üßÝ Stage 4 follow-up SHIPPED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî source_apis best-effort attribution (option 4a from AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md)
**Status:** SHIPPED (`fix/alert-audit-log-jsonb-encoding`, same PR as the P0 fix above ‚Äî found while building this). Closes the one remaining named gap in Stage 4: `source_apis` was documented as "no write-path populates this yet," with two explicitly-scoped options (4a: cheap time-window join; 4b: exact per-alert correlation ID, larger diff). Per the design doc's own recommendation, shipped 4a.

**What it does:** new `attributeSourceApis()` (`db.ts`) queries `api_telemetry_events` for provider calls in the 3 minutes before an alert fires whose `request_url` contains the alert's ticker, dedups by provider+endpoint, and flags every entry `best_effort: true` ‚Äî approximate by construction (misses calls whose URL doesn't embed the ticker, e.g. a batched market-tide pull), never claims exactness it doesn't have. Fails open to `null` on any error so a telemetry-lookup failure can never block the audit-log write it's attributing. Wired into both `insertAlertAuditLog` and `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog` ‚Äî zero call-site changes needed, exactly as 4a was scoped to require.

**Verification:** covered by the same 853/853 test run above (`buildSourceApisAttribution`'s pure-function tests). `fetchAlertAuditTrail`'s `source_api_attribution_pct` was already computed correctly from real `COUNT(source_apis)` data (no change needed there) ‚Äî it will now report a real, non-zero percentage once new alerts fire and the P0 fix above lets rows actually land.

---

## üü° P2 FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî recurring "Query read timeout" storm root-caused to unbatched admin_incidents writes
**Status:** SHIPPED (`fix/admin-incidents-batch-sync`). Multiple independent audit sweeps today (Cursor's PR #332, and this session's own `docs/api-audit/OPEN-ISSUES.md` passes 1‚Äì4) flagged a recurring cluster of generic Postgres "Query read timeout" errors ‚Äî 32/hr in one count, "22 Sentry unresolved" in another ‚Äî every sweep logged it as a P2 "watch" without ever naming the query, because the error itself carries no SQL text (it's node-postgres's own client-side `query_timeout` firing, not a Postgres-side message).

**Root cause, found via Railway runtime logs (`deploymentLogs`, `@level:error`, the documented 15:24‚Äì15:43 UTC storm window):** 111 distinct timeout errors in that window, broken out by route tag (`admin/incidents` 31, `admin/health` 14, `api-telemetry-persist` 11, `admin-audit` 9, `admin/audit-log` 6, `admin/cron-health` 5, `admin/signal-analytics` 3) ‚Äî not one query, but a cluster caused by connection-pool contention. `syncAdminIncidents()` (`src/lib/admin-incidents.ts`) issued one sequential `dbQuery()` round trip per active issue (upsert) plus one per stale-open row (resolve) ‚Äî N+M unbatched, awaited serially. It's called on **every** `/api/admin/spx/dashboard` request, which the admin UI's default "terminal" tab polls every **5 seconds** (`AdminSpxDashboard.tsx`), plus two crons (`data-integrity` */5min, `provider-health-reconcile` */10min) that call it too. With the per-replica pool capped at `max: 5` (`db.ts`) and PgBouncer skipping server-side `statement_timeout` (leaving only the driver's 35s `query_timeout` as backstop), a query merely queued for a pool slot under concurrent admin/audit load eventually throws this exact generic error ‚Äî and `isTransientPgError` doesn't match the message, so it's never retried.

**Fix:** batched both loops into single round trips. The upsert loop ‚Üí one multi-row `INSERT ... FROM unnest($1::text[], ...) ON CONFLICT` regardless of active-issue count. The resolve loop ‚Üí the namespace-ownership filtering stays an unchanged JS predicate (extracted into a new pure, unit-tested `computeIncidentsToResolve()`), but the write is now one `UPDATE ... WHERE fingerprint = ANY($1::text[])` instead of N sequential UPDATEs. Deliberately left the pool size, timeout values, and transient-error classification untouched ‚Äî this is a round-trip-count fix, not a timeout-tuning one, and the smallest change that removes the actual contention mechanism.

**Verification:** 843/843 tests (6 new for `computeIncidentsToResolve`, covering the no-scope case, active-set exclusion, both real `resolveScope` callers' prefix patterns, empty input, and the scope+active-set combination), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Confirmed the currently-live deployment shows zero of these errors in the last 20 minutes (the storm is bursty, tied to concurrent audit-sweep traffic, not constant) ‚Äî this fix reduces the round trips this specific hot path makes per poll from N+M+1 to at most 3, regardless of load.

## ‚úÖ Post-deploy live verification 2026-07-03 ‚Äî Stage 5 dry-run proposals + BIE brain banner (PRs #354, #356, #357) confirmed healthy in production

## üü¢ LOW FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî stale "single writer" doc comments (3 files) + stale cron-writer count (1 file)
**Status:** SHIPPED (`fix/stale-single-writer-comments`). Found by a background sweep agent applying the same "comment claims X, code does Y" pattern that caught the halt-banner P1 earlier this session. Both findings are documentation drift, not live bugs ‚Äî confirmed the actual runtime behavior is correct in both cases before touching anything.

**Stale "single writer" claim (`spx-lotto-engine.ts:638`, `spx-power-hour-engine.ts:535`, `src/app/api/market/lotto/today/route.ts:23`):** all three comments claimed the `spx-evaluate` cron is the sole/single writer that advances SPX lotto and power-hour state. A second real writer exists: `admin-spx-dashboard.ts`'s explicit-confirm manual mutate path (reached only after double-confirmation in the admin UI) calls `runLottoPowerHourLocked()` directly. **Not a live concurrency bug** ‚Äî that path correctly routes through the same advisory lock (`runLottoPowerHourLocked`) the cron uses, so the two writers can't double-mutate the shared record or double-fire Discord. The comments were just wrong about the writer count, which matters because a future reader trusting "single writer" could skip the lock when adding a third write path. Comments now name both writers and the shared lock that makes it safe.

**Stale cron-writer count (`market-api-auth.ts:11`):** comment claimed `isCronAuthorized()` is "the single auth gate for all 9 cron writers." Actual count of routes under `src/app/api/cron/*` using this gate (or the mixed `authorizeCronOrTierApi`) is 23, confirmed via `grep -rl` ‚Äî the file count grew as new crons shipped this session (missed-alerts, duplicate-alert checks, etc. didn't add new cron routes, but earlier growth had already outpaced the comment). Cosmetic only ‚Äî the gate itself was never wrong, just the number in its own comment.

**Verification:** 827/827 tests unchanged (comment-only diff, no logic touched), `tsc --noEmit` clean.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 5, step 1 shipped 2026-07-03 ‚Äî dry-run text proposals only, zero write/git/PR action
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-stage5-dryrun-proposals`). User explicitly picked Stage 5 ("BIE opens PRs autonomously") as the next target, then via `AskUserQuestion` chose the most conservative possible first step: dry-run plain-text proposals only ‚Äî never a diff, never a git action, never an actual PR. This is step 1 of an explicitly multi-step end-state goal, not the end-state itself.

**What it does:** `src/lib/bie/stage5-proposals.ts`'s `findStage5Proposals()` does a read-only `fs` scan of `src/components/**` (confirmed feasible in production: Railway's Nixpacks build does `COPY . /app`, so the full source tree is present in the runtime container ‚Äî verified from build logs before committing to this design), extracts exported PascalCase component names (`export function`/`export default function`/`export const =`), and flags any component whose name appears nowhere else in the codebase ‚Äî not in any other file, and not more than once within its own defining file (the second check exists because a component can be genuinely alive via an internal sub-component reference within the same file; without it, the first version of this detector produced false positives on components that ARE used, just only internally). Each flag becomes a plain-text proposal ("orphaned_component" kind, component/file/detail) ‚Äî no proposed action, no deletion, no confidence score. The module's header comment states explicitly it "NEVER writes a file, NEVER runs git, NEVER calls the GitHub API, and NEVER drafts an actual code diff."

**Manual verification against the real repo (not just unit tests):** ran the detector against the actual `src/` tree via `npx tsx -e` before shipping. Found 25 candidates after the false-positive fix; spot-checked several independently via `grep -rln <name> src/` (not trusting the detector's own logic to validate itself) ‚Äî `AuthBackground`, `Flow0dtePanel`, `BreadthPanel` (both in `GexDealerPanel.tsx`), `SpxChart`, `RouteErrorBoundary`, and `DashboardTrackRecordEmbed` all confirmed genuinely zero-referenced anywhere in the repo. None of these were deleted ‚Äî Stage 5 step 1 only surfaces the finding, a human decides what to do with it.

**Wired into:** `/api/admin/bie-report`'s new `stage5_proposals` field, a new "Proposals" panel in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (capped at 20 shown, with the count if more exist), and the roadmap. Also fixed a doc-drift bug found while updating the roadmap: `AdminBieDashboard.tsx`'s `ROADMAP` array had `n: 5` labeled "Outcome-driven calibration for plays," which collided with `docs/bie/FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`'s actual Stage 5 ("BIE opens PRs autonomously") ‚Äî the two docs had drifted from each other's numbering. Renumbered the calibration item to `n: 6` and added the correct Stage 5 entry.

**Deliberately biased toward under-reporting:** any mention of the component name anywhere (including in a comment, a string, or an unrelated context) suppresses the flag ‚Äî this is a plain substring search, not a real TypeScript import-graph resolver, so it will miss some genuinely-dead code (e.g. renamed-on-import) but will never falsely flag something that's actually wired up. Going further than this step (real draft PRs, broader or LLM-judged finding types) needs its own explicit go-ahead ‚Äî not assumed from this.

**Verification:** 833/833 tests (6 new, including a dedicated regression test for the internal-sub-component false-positive fix), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean.

---
