## üßÝ BIE Stage 2 fully closed 2026-07-03 ‚Äî duplicate-alert detection shipped, zero invented ground truth
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-duplicate-alert-detection`). Last open item from Stage 2's original ask ("duplicate/incorrect alerts" ‚Äî "incorrect" was already covered by outcome grading). User said "keep pushing" after Stage 2/3 completion, so this picked the highest-value next target instead of waiting to be told what to build next.

**Approach:** rather than inventing a new dedup-key definition (the exact reason this was deferred as "a distinct dedup-key design problem" in the original Stage 4 scoping), this verifies `alert_audit_log`'s OWN already-documented design invariant against production reality ‚Äî the table's whole point (`docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`) is exactly one row per `(alert_type, source_key)`, enforced by three different mechanisms built earlier tonight (0DTE `xmax = 0`, Night Hawk published `xmax = 0`, Night Hawk rejected partial unique index). `fetchDuplicateAlertGroups()` (`db.ts`) is a `GROUP BY (alert_type, source_key) HAVING COUNT(*) > 1` ‚Äî if it ever returns a row, one of those three dedup mechanisms has a bug. Zero new definition invented; it's a correctness check on work already shipped this session.

**Also checked, not built:** GEX regime-alert push notifications (`gex-alerts` cron) already have their own per-day Redis dedup (`gex-alert-sent:{ticker}:{type}:{date}`) ‚Äî reviewed the route and found this already well-designed, so no duplicate work needed there. (Noted, not fixed: the check-then-act pattern between the Redis dedup read and the push send isn't atomic, a narrow theoretical race under concurrent cron overlap ‚Äî no evidence this has ever happened, not chased without a real signal.)

**Wired into:** `/api/admin/bie-report`'s new `duplicate_alerts` field, surfaced in the existing "Audit trail" admin panel (reads the same table the audit-trail rows come from, so it lives right next to them).

**Verification:** 827/827 tests (unchanged ‚Äî `fetchDuplicateAlertGroups` is a thin DB-read wrapper, same no-unit-test precedent as `fetchAlertAuditTrail`/`getDatabasePoolStats`), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Not exercised against live Postgres from this sandbox; the honest expected result is zero duplicate groups, which itself would be a positive confirmation that all three Stage 4 dedup mechanisms are holding ‚Äî will read the live `/api/admin/bie-report` response once deployed.

## üî¥ P1 FIXED + üßÝ BIE Stage 2 & 3 completed 2026-07-03 ‚Äî dbQuery double-counting bug found and fixed, missed-alerts detection shipped, all Railway/Postgres Stage 3 items closed
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-railway-resource-envvar-log-discovery`). User asked to complete BIE Stage 2 and Stage 3 today; per explicit direction, missed-alerts detection uses a cron-outage-only ground truth (not a full historical backtest), and the Postgres slow-query check is check-only (never attempts to enable the extension).

**P1 found and fixed: `error_events` double-counting.** Stage 2's "database query failures" item was already marked SHIPPED from an earlier PR today (`2e19dc3`, #321) that added a centralized `captureError()` call inside `dbQuery()`'s final-failure path ‚Äî but that PR's own audit comment claimed "checked that none of the 19 direct call sites already wrap failures in their own captureError, so this can't double-count," which does not hold. Independent re-audit found `dbQuery()` has ~74 call sites across 32 files (not 19), and several admin routes' catch-all handler (`recordAdminRouteError`, `admin-route-errors.ts`) independently re-captures the SAME failure under a second source (`admin_route`) whenever a `dbQuery` rejection propagates up uncaught ‚Äî confirmed for at least 4 routes (`admin/audit-log`, `admin/signal-analytics`, `admin/incidents`, `admin/spx/dashboard`). This inflates the exact error count BIE's own discovery report uses to say "N errors in 24h ‚Äî elevated," directly undermining the "never invent/overclaim a correctness verdict" charter by polluting BIE's own signal with duplicates.

**Fix:** WeakSet-based dedup marker in `error-sink.ts` (`markDbQueryCaptured`/`wasDbQueryCaptured`), keyed on the error object's identity (verified the object reference survives unwrapped from `dbQuery()`'s throw to these routes' catch blocks ‚Äî no re-wrapping in between). `dbQuery()`'s `reportQueryFailure()` marks each error it captures; `recordAdminRouteError` skips its own `captureError` call when the error was already marked, while still doing everything else (in-memory error list, console.error, `recordApiCall` telemetry) unconditionally ‚Äî so genuinely non-`dbQuery` admin-route errors are still captured normally. Does NOT touch `dbQuery()`'s own capture logic, which was correct.

**Stage 2 ‚Äî missed alerts, SHIPPED.** New `src/lib/bie/missed-alerts.ts`: `detectMissedAlertWindows()` flags only the market-hours-only crons that themselves PRODUCE a member alert (`flow-ingest`, `spx-evaluate`, `gex-alerts`) being currently failed or stale during RTH ‚Äî deliberately excludes cache warmers (`grid-warm`, `heatmap-warm`, `nights-watch-warm` just pre-warm a read cache) and validators (`data-correctness` confirms state, doesn't alert). Reuses `admin-cron-health.ts`'s existing `market_hours_stale` flag ‚Äî zero new schema, zero new access. Wired into `runBieDiscovery()`'s narrative and `/api/admin/bie-report`'s structured `missed_alerts` field.

**Stage 3 ‚Äî Railway resource usage / env-var audit / runtime logs, all SHIPPED.** `src/lib/railway-status.ts` gained three new probes, all read-only:
- `probeRailwayResourceUsage()` ‚Äî Railway's `metrics(measurements: [CPU_USAGE, MEMORY_USAGE_GB], ...)` query, confirmed live during investigation.
- `probeRailwayEnvVars()` ‚Äî Railway's `variables(...)` query returns actual key‚Üívalue pairs; the probe extracts key names on the very next line and never touches, logs, or returns the values again. Reports total count + which hand-kept `CRITICAL_ENV_VARS` are missing. Staleness (last-changed timestamp) is confirmed NOT exposed by Railway's API ‚Äî not built, not guessed.
- `probeRailwayRuntimeErrors()` ‚Äî first automated read of runtime logs (not just deploy metadata): finds the deployment actually serving traffic via `pickLiveDeploymentId()` (first `SUCCESS` in a newest-first list ‚Äî the newest entry can be a stuck `BUILDING` deploy, exactly like tonight's earlier Railway status-reporting-stall finding), then queries `deploymentLogs(filter: "@level:error")` over a rolling window.

**Stage 3 ‚Äî Postgres slow-query log, CHECKED (not enabled, per explicit instruction to check only).** New `src/lib/pg-stat-statements-health.ts`'s `probePgStatStatements()` queries `pg_extension` for presence; reports `enabled: true` + tracked-statement count if found, `enabled: false` otherwise. Deliberately never attempts `CREATE EXTENSION` ‚Äî that's a server-level Postgres config change (needs `shared_preload_libraries` set at the server, may need a restart) left to the user's explicit go-ahead.

**Wired into the admin UI:** new "Infra" panel in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (CPU/memory, runtime error count, env-var audit, pg_stat_statements status) and a "Missed alerts" header chip.

**Verification:** 827/827 tests (14 new: 4 dbQuery-dedup, 6 missed-alerts, 8 Railway probe pure-function tests, 1 pg_stat_statements not-configured), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean (caught nothing new this time ‚Äî the Stage 4 query-surface work earlier tonight already established the pattern). Railway GraphQL queries (`metrics`, `variables`, `deploymentLogs` with severity filter) were validated live against the real API during investigation, not just written against docs. `pg_stat_statements`'s actual enabled/disabled state on the production instance is unverified from this sandbox (blocked from direct Postgres access) ‚Äî will read from the live `/api/admin/bie-report` response post-deploy.

---

## üü° OBSERVED 2026-07-03 17:44-18:1x UTC ‚Äî Railway deployment status API stuck reporting BUILDING ~25+ min after the build genuinely finished; no user-facing impact
**Status:** OBSERVED, no code fix (this is Railway's own control-plane, not our app). Deployment `aecb3c44` (commit `2b4d6ba`, PR #347) built cleanly ‚Äî `buildLogs` show a successful Next.js build and container image export (`containerimage.digest` emitted) at 17:46:56 UTC ‚Äî but the deployment's `status` field stayed `BUILDING` with `statusUpdatedAt` frozen at `17:44:25.760Z` for at least 25 minutes afterward, with zero new build-log lines in that window (confirmed via 4 separate polls spaced minutes apart, not a single stale read).

**Why this isn't a P0:** `GET /api/ready` on the live site stayed healthy and fast (200 OK, ~0.5-0.7s) throughout the entire stall. The prior deployment (`928d265f`, commit `601f3e6`, PR #345) shows confirmed `SUCCESS` and was almost certainly still serving live traffic the whole time ‚Äî Railway's rollout didn't cut over to the stuck deployment, so members saw zero disruption.

**Root cause:** unknown ‚Äî this is Railway's control-plane, not app code. `canRedeploy`/`canRollback` both read `false` on the stuck deployment, so there's no API-level remediation available from this sandbox; this needs either Railway resolving it server-side or the user checking the Railway dashboard directly if it doesn't clear on its own.

**Action:** none from the app side ‚Äî build output was correct and the site was never down. Logged per the standing instruction to dig into Railway build/deploy logs for real issues, same as the earlier Query-read-timeout investigation. Will re-check next time a `src/**` PR needs a deploy-confirmed merge; not worth dedicating further polling cycles to this specific stuck deployment record.

## üî¥ P1 FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî Halt-feed-degraded banner (and Largo's prompt context) claimed entries are "blocked" when the engine has always failed OPEN, never closed
**Status:** FIXED (`fix/halt-feed-banner-false-claim`). Prompted by PR #332 (Cursor's audit) flagging "Halt feed offline" as a live observation ‚Äî investigated whether that reflected a real current block, not just a cosmetic banner.

**Root cause:** `SpxDashboard.tsx`'s banner has said "Halt feed offline ‚Äî entries blocked until reconnect" since it was introduced (`1c0bca7`, PR #103, 2026-06-30) ‚Äî the SAME commit that introduced `spx-play-gates.ts`, whose `shouldBlockForTradingHalt(undefined, { failClosedOnStale: false })` call has *always* explicitly failed open on a stale channel (comment in that file: "a transient UW WS gap during RTH would block all entries even when no halt existed... proceeding fail-open with a warning"). The banner copy and the actual gate logic were written in the same PR but never reconciled ‚Äî the banner has been factually wrong about the system's own behavior since day one, not a regression. Grepped every `shouldBlockForTradingHalt` call site (2 total, `spx-play-gates.ts` and `nighthawk/dossier.ts`) ‚Äî both pass `failClosedOnStale: false`; the fail-closed branch is dead code in production.

**Worse instance, same root cause:** `largo-live-feed.ts`'s prompt-context builder fed Largo's own model context the line "Entry signals are blocked fail-closed until reconnection. Inform the user if they ask about entering a position" whenever `channel_stale` was true ‚Äî meaning Largo could actively tell a paying member they can't enter a position when the real system allows it (with just a manual-verify caution). This directly violates the platform's "BIE/AI must never invent a correctness verdict, only report what validation already found" charter, since it invented a block that was never true.

**Compounding issue:** the UW `trading_halts` channel is event-only (silent unless a symbol actually halts) and its staleness proxy (`isUwHaltSourceStale` in `uw-socket.ts`) reads off the freshest message across ALL UW channels ‚Äî which naturally goes quiet off-hours/holidays. The `SpxDashboard.tsx` banner had no session-active gate, so it would also flash amber during every off-hours/holiday visit for a channel that has nothing to report, not just when genuinely degraded during RTH.

**Fix:** new dependency-free `shouldShowHaltDegradedBanner()` (`src/lib/spx-halt-banner.ts` ‚Äî deliberately NOT added to `spx-play-gates.ts`, which transitively imports `uw-socket.ts`'s server-only chain into Postgres/telemetry and broke the client bundle on first attempt) gates the banner on `sessionActive && haltChannelStale && activeHaltsCount === 0`. Banner copy corrected to "Halt feed degraded ‚Äî proceeding fail-open; verify no active halts before entering". `largo-live-feed.ts`'s prompt line corrected to state the engine fails open and ask the user to manually verify. `learn/guides/instruments/spx-slayer.ts`'s member-facing education copy (3 spots) corrected to match ‚Äî it repeated the same "blocks entries"/"no-new-risk until reconnect" claim.

**What was deliberately left unchanged:** the real `TRADING HALT` banner (a confirmed active halt) is untouched ‚Äî that one genuinely blocks and the copy for it was already accurate. Did not touch `spx-play-gates.ts`'s actual gate logic (already correct, fail-open, `failClosedOnStale: false`) ‚Äî this was purely a copy/UI-gating fix, zero behavior change to what already blocks or doesn't.

**Verification:** 807/807 tests (4 new: `shouldShowHaltDegradedBanner` covers off-hours-hides, active-session-shows, fresh-channel-hides, active-halt-takes-precedence), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean (build caught the client-bundle break on the first attempt ‚Äî moving the function out of `spx-play-gates.ts` fixed it). Not exercised against a live stale-channel scenario from this sandbox (would need to simulate a UW WS gap during RTH); the fix is a pure function + static copy, verified by inspection and fixture tests.

---

**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-stage4-query-surface`). This was the last remaining piece of Stage 4 (`docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`): schema and all three write-paths (0DTE, Night Hawk published, Night Hawk rejected) were already live, but nothing read `alert_audit_log` back out ‚Äî it was write-only.

**Fix:** new `fetchAlertAuditTrail()` (`db.ts`) runs three read-only queries in parallel ‚Äî last 20 rows, `GROUP BY alert_type` counts, and a `source_apis IS NOT NULL` coverage ratio ‚Äî and returns them as one summary. Wired into `/api/admin/bie-report`'s new `audit_trail` field (same fail-open `.catch(() => null)` pattern as every other probe on that route) and rendered as a new "Audit trail" panel in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` (recent-rows table + per-type counts + attribution note).

Surfaced as a real computed field rather than baked into static prose, so the day a write-path starts populating it, the panel reflects that with zero code changes here ‚Äî and BIE never claims a coverage number it can't back, per the platform's Stage-4-adjacent "never invent a correctness verdict" charter.

**Verification:** 803/803 tests (unchanged ‚Äî this function needs a live Postgres to test meaningfully, same precedent as `getDatabasePoolStats`/`fetchDiscoveryIncidents`, neither of which has a unit test either), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Not exercised against a live Postgres from this sandbox; will confirm live via the admin panel once deployed.

**Stage 4 status:** fully shipped ‚Äî schema, all three write-paths, and the query surface.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 4: Night Hawk rejected-play write-path shipped ‚Äî all three audit-trail write-paths now live
**Status:** SHIPPED (`feat/bie-nighthawk-rejected-writepath`). `generateEditionPlays()` (`claude-edition.ts`) now returns `geometryRejected: Array<{ticker, drops, play}>` instead of only `console.warn`ing it. `edition-builder.ts` calls the new `recordNighthawkRejectedAuditTrail()` immediately after destructuring the result ‚Äî before any of the function's existing early-return branches ‚Äî so a rejection is recorded regardless of whether the run ultimately publishes anything (a rejected play is never written anywhere else, so this is its only record).

**Why now:** re-evaluated fresh (re-read both files, didn't rely on stale context) per explicit instruction to give an honest attemptable-or-defer verdict. The insertion point is purely additive ‚Äî it doesn't touch any existing branch/condition in either function ‚Äî and the dedup index (`idx_alert_audit_log_nighthawk_rejected_dedup`) was already shipped and live, so the only remaining risk (duplicate rows on a `force`-rebuild re-deriving the same rejections) was already closed.

**Fix:** new pure `buildNighthawkRejectedAuditRow()` in `play-outcomes.ts` cites the real `validatePlayGeometry()` drop reasons as individual `decision_trace` entries (never fabricated) and sets `final_output: null` (a rejected play was never member-visible, so there is no real final output to record). `insertNighthawkRejectedAuditLog()` (`db.ts`) uses `dbQuery()`, not raw `pool.query()` ‚Äî matching PR #341's retry-safety fix on the sibling `insertAlertAuditLog()`, so a transient PgBouncer blip after the geometry check doesn't silently drop the rejection record. The checkpoint-restore path still has no rejection data by construction (unchanged, documented limitation, not a regression ‚Äî it resumes from an already-vetted checkpoint that never ran geometry validation in that run).

**Verification:** 801/801 tests (2 new fixture tests: real multi-reason SHORT rejection, and a corrupt-entry-range LONG rejection), `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Not exercised against a live Postgres from this sandbox ‚Äî same limitation as every other write-path in this doc; correctness reviewed by inspection + fixtures, confirmed live post-deploy via the next real Night Hawk edition that rejects a play on geometry.

**Stage 4 status:** all three write-paths (0DTE, Night Hawk published, Night Hawk rejected) are now shipped. Only the query-surface PR (`/api/admin/bie-report` `audit_trail` block) remains ‚Äî see `docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`.

## üü° P2 FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî BIE router (`bie-router` answer path) skipped Layer 4 `verifyClaims()` ‚Äî `claims_total`/`claims_verified` always null in telemetry
**Status:** FIXED (PR #340). Cursor audit found `runLargoQuery` / `runLargoQueryStream` logged `claims_total: null` for every deterministic router answer while the Claude fallback path ran full Layer 4 verification. Root cause: `tryBieRoute()` returned only the composed markdown string; the source payloads used by `composeBieAnswer()` were discarded before logging.

**Fix:** `composeBieAnswer()` now returns `{ answer, context }` (raw board/tool payload). Both Largo entry points call `collectContextNumbers(context)` + `verifyClaims(answer, ctxNumbers)` before `logBie()`, matching the Claude path. Deterministic answers built from the same readers as the dashboards should verify at ~100% by construction; the telemetry now records that instead of nulls.

**Files:** `src/lib/bie/composers.ts`, `src/lib/largo-terminal.ts`, `src/lib/bie/bie.test.ts` (router play-line verification regression).

**Verification:** 798/798 tests, `tsc --noEmit` clean. Live post-deploy: query BIE with "How are today's plays doing?" and confirm `bie_interactions.claims_total IS NOT NULL` for `answer_source = 'bie-router'`.

## üü° INVESTIGATED 2026-07-03 15:4x UTC ‚Äî "Query read timeout" storm across admin endpoints is real and ongoing, most likely caused by concurrent dual-agent audit load hitting a deliberately small per-replica connection pool, not a code defect
**Status:** INVESTIGATED, root cause understood, no speculative code change made. Pulled Railway `deploymentLogs` directly for the currently-live deployment (`c69b6c93`, live since 14:36 UTC) at the user's request to check build/deploy logs for issues ‚Äî found **301 of the last 501 log lines were `error` severity**, dominated by `Query read timeout` across `admin/incidents`, `admin/health`, `admin-audit`, `admin/cron-health`, `admin/audit-log`, `admin/signal-analytics`, `api-telemetry-persist`, `cron/db-cleanup`, and the `[db] query failed while already reporting a failure` recursion-guard message (from PR #321). Timestamps span continuously from 15:24 to 15:43 UTC (essentially "now" at investigation time) ‚Äî **this supersedes the earlier conclusion that the ~11:29-11:44 UTC burst was a resolved one-off blip: it is not resolved, it is ongoing.**

**What it is NOT:** not caused by the holiday-gate bug (PR #331) ‚Äî that bug produced a false correctness *flag*, not a query failure, and the timeout pattern predates and postdates that fix. Not a "DB fully down" scenario ‚Äî `/api/ready` (the member-facing critical-path health check) has responded in 0.2-0.6s on every check tonight, including during these bursts. The failures are concentrated entirely in **admin-panel/telemetry/cron-housekeeping endpoints**, never in member-facing `/api/market/*` reads.

**Most likely root cause (mechanical, from reading `db.ts`, not guessed):** the Postgres pool is deliberately small ‚Äî `max: parseInt(process.env.PG_POOL_MAX ?? "5", 10)` **per replica** ‚Äî with the comment explaining why: "PgBouncer sits in front of Postgres on Railway... we keep our own pool small... PgBouncer multiplexes these to many clients." This service runs **5 replicas** (`iad: 3, us-west2: 2` per the Railway service manifest), so up to 25 client connections can be in flight through a single shared PgBouncer at once. The connection string routes through `thomas.proxy.rlwy.net` (matches `connectionViaPooler()`'s `proxy.rlwy` check), so the server-enforced `statement_timeout` is skipped (PgBouncer rejects it as a startup param) and only the driver-side `query_timeout` (`PG_STATEMENT_TIMEOUT_MS` + 5000ms = 35s by default) actually bounds a query ‚Äî a query merely *queued* waiting for a PgBouncer backend slot under load would eventually breach 35s and throw the exact generic "Query read timeout" seen everywhere, regardless of which specific query it was.

**Why tonight specifically:** this session and Cursor's session have both been running repeated full-audit scripts (`full-site-deep-audit.mjs`, `data-validator.mjs`-equivalent, `rth-browser-test.mjs`, direct `?force=1` cron probes) against the **same** admin/cron endpoints for hours, on top of each replica's own scheduled cron-health/incident checks. Two AI agents concurrently hammering the same small, shared connection pool is a load pattern that would not occur under normal single-admin-viewer usage ‚Äî self-inflicted by the audit activity itself, not a pre-existing production bug from tonight's code changes.

**Why no code fix shipped:** bumping `PG_POOL_MAX` without visibility into PgBouncer's actual backend pool size to real Postgres could make contention worse, not better (more client-side connections competing for the same constrained backend slots) ‚Äî that would be exactly the kind of unverified, speculative change the standing "never invent, verify before fixing" principle warns against. The responsible move right now is to (a) document the real mechanism, (b) stop being part of the problem, and (c) leave the actual pool/timeout tuning to a follow-up with real backend-connection visibility (Postgres `pg_stat_activity`, PgBouncer's own stats ‚Äî none of which this sandbox can reach).

**Action taken:** throttling this session's own verification cadence going forward ‚Äî spot-checking `/api/ready` for basic health rather than re-running the full `full-site-deep-audit.mjs` suite (which itself fires 3 concurrent cron probes) after every single deploy, reserving the full suite for genuinely significant changes. Flagged to Cursor (comment on PR #332) that their own tooling has direct DB access this sandbox lacks, in case they can pull `pg_stat_activity`/PgBouncer stats directly to confirm or refute the pool-contention hypothesis with real numbers.

**Update 2026-07-04 ‚Äî the ceiling modeled above was 3x too low, and PgBouncer's real backend budget was documented all along:** this entry's "up to 25 client connections... through a single shared PgBouncer" used the code DEFAULT (`PG_POOL_MAX ?? "5"`, √ó5 replicas = 25). `docs/PGBOUNCER-SETUP.md` (written the same day, apparently never cross-referenced back into this entry) documents the actual PRODUCTION override: `PG_POOL_MAX=15` per replica √ó 5 replicas = **75** client connections against PgBouncer's own documented `DEFAULT_POOL_SIZE=20` backend budget ‚Äî a genuine 3.75x oversubscription, not the "self-inflicted by concurrent audit load" story concluded here. The CEO/CTO production audit (`docs/audit/CEO-CTO-AUDIT-20260704.md`, finding `db.ts:119`) caught the doc/code cross-reference this entry missed. Fixed in PR #439: `PG_POOL_MAX`'s fallback default is now computed from the documented budget √∑ `REPLICA_COUNT` instead of a flat guess, an explicit override that would still oversubscribe now logs a visible warning instead of failing silently, and `getDatabasePoolStats().waiting` is wired into the admin health snapshot as a leading indicator ‚Äî see the dedicated FIXED entry above for the full writeup. This doesn't retroactively prove pool exhaustion (vs. concurrent audit load) caused tonight's specific timeout storm, but it means the ceiling really was tighter than modeled, and the gap is now visible instead of requiring a manual doc cross-reference to notice.

## üî¥ P0 FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî `isSpxRthActive`/`isSpxEngineCronWindow` had no holiday calendar check; six crons + the SPX desk's own market-open signal ran/reported "open" on today's NYSE holiday
**Status:** FIXED. User-flagged via Railway log screenshots (a burst of `[db] Query read timeout` errors across `admin-audit`/`admin/incidents`/`admin/health`/`api-telemetry-persist`/`cron-staleness-watchdog` around 11:29-11:44 UTC) ‚Äî investigated that cluster first, then noticed a second, independent, still-live problem while cross-checking recent deploys: Cursor's PR #330 (merged 14:36 UTC, "holiday-aware RTH gate clears false flow-correctness flags on NYSE holidays") fixed the exact same *class* of bug in `isEtCashRth()`/`run-correctness.ts`, which prompted checking whether the sibling `data-integrity` validator had the identical gap. It did, live: `curl /api/cron/data-integrity?force=1` returned `market_open: true` and a false P0 (`"GEX SPY cold during RTH"`) on today's Independence-Day-observed holiday. Reproduced twice via `full-site-deep-audit.mjs` before treating it as real (learned that lesson from the earlier transient cron-watchdog flag tonight) ‚Äî this one reproduced consistently, not a blip.

**Root cause:** `isSpxRthActive()` (`spx-market-session.ts`) ‚Äî the SPX desk's own RTH/`market_open` determination, used by `buildSpxDeskPulse()` ‚Äî checks weekday + either Polygon's live `/v1/marketstatus/now` status or a naive clock-time fallback, but had **zero holiday-calendar awareness in either branch**. Polygon's own status endpoint does not appear to flag this specific holiday as closed (or the status call intermittently fails and falls through to the naive fallback, which also has no holiday check) ‚Äî either way, at 9:30am-4pm ET on today's holiday, `isSpxRthActive` returned `true`. That `market_open: true` flows into `data-integrity-checks.ts`'s `runDataIntegrityChecks()`, which then genuinely ran its cross-tool GEX check and got a real "no matrix" result (correct ‚Äî there IS no fresh GEX data off-hours/holiday, as established many times tonight) but reported it as a P0 discrepancy instead of correctly skipping.

**Wider blast radius than the audit script:** grepped every consumer of the sibling `isSpxEngineCronWindow()` (`spx-play-session-guards.ts`) ‚Äî same missing-holiday-check shape ‚Äî and found it bare-gates **six** cron routes with no `force` flag needed: `spx-evaluate`, `data-integrity`, `data-correctness`, `spx-signal-observe`, `market-regime-detector`, `provider-health-reconcile`. Railway's cron scheduler fires these on fixed wall-clock windows regardless of the trading calendar, so all six were very likely running real work on today's holiday, not just my manual `?force=1` probe. Also affects the SPX Slayer desk's own member-visible `market_status`/`market_label` fields (via the same `isSpxRthActive`), which could have shown "RTH OPEN" instead of "CLOSED" on a holiday ‚Äî a genuinely member-facing correctness issue, not just an internal audit false-positive.

**Fix:** added the same holiday gate Cursor's PR used (`isTradingDayEt(formatEtDate(now))` from `nighthawk/session.ts`, the existing `US_MARKET_HOLIDAYS` source of truth) to both functions at their single shared choke points ‚Äî `isSpxRthActive()` (fixes the desk pulse + `data-integrity`) and `isSpxEngineCronWindow()` (fixes all six cron call sites in one place, DRY, instead of patching six route files individually). Checked for circular imports before adding (`nighthawk/session.ts`'s own import chain is two leaf modules deep in both directions) ‚Äî confirmed clean via `tsc`/tests/build, not just the ad-hoc script that gave a false positive earlier tonight. No open 0DTE play can exist from a non-trading day, so gating `isSpxEngineCronWindow`'s post-close force-flatten tail on the same check is safe.

**Verification:** new `spx-market-session.test.ts` (4 tests: holiday-with-Polygon-reporting-open, holiday-with-no-status/fallback-path, real-trading-day-still-true, `marketStatusLabel` returns CLOSED not RTH OPEN on the holiday) + 3 new tests in `spx-play-session-guards.test.ts` for `isSpxEngineCronWindow`. 797/797 total tests, `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. Re-ran `full-site-deep-audit.mjs` and the direct `data-integrity?force=1` query post-deploy to confirm the P0 clears ‚Äî see the post-deploy verification entry below this one.

**On the original Query-read-timeout screenshots:** those predate this fix (11:29-11:44 UTC, well before Cursor's 14:36 UTC deploy) and are unrelated to this holiday-gate bug. They span many unrelated endpoints simultaneously (`admin-audit`, `api-telemetry-persist`, `admin/incidents`, `admin/health`, `cron-staleness-watchdog`) ‚Äî the signature of a genuine connection-pool disruption rather than a code bug in any one handler. Notably, one screenshot shows `[db] query failed while already reporting a failure ‚Äî DB likely fully down` ‚Äî the exact re-entrancy-guard message added in tonight's earlier dbQuery-capture fix (PR #321) ‚Äî confirming that guard fired correctly under real load rather than looping. **Correction:** initially concluded this was a resolved one-off blip since spot-checks were clean afterward ‚Äî that was wrong. A deeper log pull (see the entry directly above this one) found the same pattern still running continuously as of 15:43 UTC. Superseded by that entry's fuller investigation and root-cause hypothesis (per-replica pool size under concurrent dual-agent audit load) ‚Äî kept here only for the original timeline/evidence, not as the current conclusion.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 3: Railway deploy status wired into `runBieDiscovery`'s report ‚Äî first automated use of the API

**Fix:** new `src/lib/railway-status.ts` ‚Äî `probeRailwayStatus()`, a one-shot read-only GraphQL query for the last 5 deployments (status/commit/timestamp), gated behind all four required env vars being present (mirrors `probeRedisHealth()`'s `configured: false` fallback exactly). Never mutates anything ‚Äî no redeploy, no env var reads/writes, no log access (explicitly a separate, larger surface left for later per the existing Stage 3 table in `docs/bie/FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`). Wired into `/api/admin/bie-report` as a sibling live snapshot alongside `redis`/`db_pool` (the established pattern ‚Äî live infra probes are point-in-time snapshots computed at request time, not baked into `runBieDiscovery()`'s persisted narrative text). Surfaced in `AdminBieDashboard.tsx` as a new "Railway deploy" status chip (amber only on a real `FAILED`/`CRASHED`/probe-error state, same tone logic as the existing Redis chip).

**Verification:** 4 new fixture tests in `railway-status.test.ts` ‚Äî the pure `mapDeploymentEdges()` mapper (real fields extracted, missing fields become `null` not fabricated, `undefined` input never throws) plus one live-behavior test confirming `probeRailwayStatus()` returns `{ configured: false }` immediately (no network attempt) when `RAILWAY_TOKEN` is unset. 789/789 tests, `tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` clean. Frontend chip is code/type-verified only ‚Äî sandbox browser is blocked, so it has not been visually rendered or clicked through; needs a real browser pass.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 4: Night Hawk write-path (published half) shipped ‚Äî scoped narrower than the design doc on purpose
**Status:** SHIPPED. Fourth step of the 5-step Stage 4 rollout. Deliberately split from the design doc's original single-PR scope ("published plays AND `validatePlayGeometry()` rejections") into two: this PR ships only the **published** half; the **rejected** half is explicit follow-up, not silently dropped.

**Why split:** the rejected-play half needs `generateEditionPlays()` (`claude-edition.ts`) to return its `geometryRejected` list (currently only `console.warn`'d, never returned) and that list threaded through `edition-builder.ts`'s two different code paths into `finalPlays` ‚Äî a fresh-generation path AND a checkpoint-restore path that bypasses geometry validation entirely (it loads already-vetted plays from a prior run's checkpoint, so no rejection data exists on that path). That's a real signature change across a ~800-line function with backfill/retry/Slack-notification side effects, on a night markets are closed and the sandbox browser is blocked ‚Äî not something to rush through untested. The published half has no such entanglement: it only touches `db.ts` and `play-outcomes.ts`, mirrors the already-shipped, already-verified 0DTE pattern, and is exactly as additive/low-risk as that PR was.

**Fix ‚Äî same `xmax = 0` pattern, reused, not re-invented:**
- `upsertNighthawkPlayOutcomes` (`src/lib/db.ts`) now returns `Promise<Set<string>>` (was `Promise<void>`) ‚Äî tickers freshly INSERTed this call. Its existing `ON CONFLICT (edition_for, ticker) DO UPDATE ... WHERE outcome = 'pending'` guard composes correctly with `RETURNING (xmax = 0) AS inserted`: Postgres returns no row at all for a conflict where the `WHERE` clause is false (an already-graded row hit by a stale force-rebuild), so that case is correctly excluded from "freshly published" too ‚Äî not just the ordinary refresh case. Confirmed this table is genuinely re-upserted more than once per edition: `play-outcomes.ts`'s own comment documents a per-edition lock guarding against "concurrent force-rebuilds racing on the same upsert."
- New pure `buildNighthawkAuditRow(play, editionFor, sector)` in `play-outcomes.ts` (co-located with `syncNighthawkPlayOutcomes`, the direct analog of `persistZeroDteScan`). Scope is intentionally narrower than 0DTE's: the individual gate verdicts (geometry/premium-cap/strike-validation) are computed upstream in `claude-edition.ts` and not yet threaded down to this call site, so `decision_trace` only records the one check this function can verify honestly on its own ‚Äî whether target/stop parsed ‚Äî rather than fabricating pass/fail for gates it has no visibility into. `final_output` mirrors the actual member-visible card fields (thesis, key_signal, entry_range, target, stop, options_play).
- `syncNighthawkPlayOutcomes` fire-and-forgets one `insertAlertAuditLog()` per freshly-published ticker only ‚Äî a force-rebuild refresh of an already-published play writes zero new audit rows, same discipline as the 0DTE side.

**Blast radius:** only `db.ts` and `nighthawk/play-outcomes.ts` touched. `claude-edition.ts`/`edition-builder.ts` untouched ‚Äî the rejected-play half stays a named follow-up in `docs/bie/AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`.

**Verification:** 2 new fixture tests in `play-outcomes.test.ts` (same fixture-cast style the file already uses for `resolveOutcome`/`parsePlayLevels`): a normal play with parseable levels records `passed: true`, and a play with unparseable target/stop ("see levels" / "-") honestly records `passed: false` rather than guessing. 785/785 tests, `tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` clean. Same live-verification caveat as the 0DTE PR: today is a market holiday, so no edition publish runs tonight to exercise this ‚Äî flagged for a Monday-morning check that `alert_audit_log` gets nighthawk rows after the next edition ships.

## ‚úÖ Post-deploy verification 2026-07-03 12:41 UTC ‚Äî 0DTE write-path (PR #325) live, no regression

## üßÝ BIE Stage 4: 0DTE write-path shipped ‚Äî `alert_audit_log` now populated at first flag, additive-only
**Status:** SHIPPED. Third step of the 5-step Stage 4 rollout (design doc ‚Üí schema PR #316 ‚Üí **this PR** ‚Üí Night Hawk write-path ‚Üí query-surface). Re-evaluated the earlier "too risky with markets closed" deferral per an explicit prompt to reconsider ‚Äî reading `persistZeroDteScan` end-to-end showed the actual change is purely additive (one extra audit row using data the scanner already computed), not a modification to any gate/scoring/decision logic, so the original caution was overstated. Fixture-tested, same pattern the rest of `zerodte/board.ts` already uses ‚Äî no live market data needed to build or verify this.

**Design problem solved:** `persistZeroDteScan` runs on *every* scan cycle, not once per new flag ‚Äî before the 15:00 ET cutoff `eligible` includes both brand-new setups and existing ones being refreshed within the session. Writing an audit row per call would create near-duplicate rows for the same logical alert as it refreshes throughout the day, defeating the trail's purpose (capturing decision context at the moment the alert first fired).

**Fix ‚Äî insert-vs-update detection, then gate the write on it:**
- `upsertZeroDteSetupLog` (`src/lib/db.ts`) now returns `Promise<Set<string>>` (was `Promise<void>`) ‚Äî the tickers that were a **fresh INSERT** this call, detected via the standard Postgres `RETURNING (xmax = 0) AS inserted` idiom (`xmax` is unset on a brand-new row; `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` sets it on a refresh). Zero other callers exist (`grep -rn upsertZeroDteSetupLog src` ‚Üí only `db.ts` def + `scan.ts` call site), so the signature change is safe.
- `persistZeroDteScan` (`src/lib/zerodte/scan.ts`) filters `eligible` down to `freshlyFlagged` tickers and fire-and-forgets one `insertAlertAuditLog()` call per genuinely-new setup ‚Äî refresh ticks write zero audit rows.
- New pure `buildZeroDteAuditRow(setup, sessionDate)` (`src/lib/zerodte/board.ts`, exported alongside a new `ZeroDteAuditRow` type) builds the row from a setup + session date ‚Äî no I/O, so it's fixture-testable. `decision_trace` cites the **real** gate values against the **real** exported thresholds (`SETUP_MIN_GROSS`, `SETUP_MIN_AGGR_SHARE`, `SETUP_MIN_DOMINANCE`, `SETUP_MAX_ITM_PCT` ‚Äî now exported from `board.ts` instead of module-private, so the audit trail can't silently drift from the live gate values) and recomputes `passed` from the setup's actual fields rather than hardcoding `true` ‚Äî honest even if a future setup somehow reaches this function without having cleared a gate. `input_snapshot` carries the score/premium/spike/intraday-conflict fields the scanner already computed; `final_output` mirrors the attached contract plan (or `null` if none exists yet ‚Äî never guessed).
- New `insertAlertAuditLog()` in `db.ts` ‚Äî a thin, best-effort INSERT (fire-and-forget from the caller, logs a warning and does not throw on failure) so an audit-trail write can never break the scanner.

**Blast radius:** only `db.ts`, `zerodte/board.ts`, `zerodte/scan.ts` touched. Night Hawk's write-path is a separate table/call chain (`nighthawk_play_outcomes`) ‚Äî explicitly out of scope for this PR, tracked as the next Stage 4 step.

**Verification:** 3 new fixture tests in `board.test.ts` (built via the existing `row()`/`deriveZeroDteSetups()`/`enrichSetup()` helpers already used by the rest of the file ‚Äî no new test infra): all-gates-passed + correct `source_key`/`alert_type`, spike vs non-spike `trigger_reason`, and `confidence_score` preferring the full dossier score over the raw evidence score when a dossier is present. 783/783 tests, `tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` clean. The `xmax = 0` insert-detection SQL itself is not exercised by a test (no DB in this sandbox) ‚Äî flagged for a live post-deploy check: confirm `alert_audit_log` gets exactly one row per new 0DTE flag once markets reopen Monday, not one per refresh tick.

## üü° FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî same log-noise class found in a second place, swept for more before stopping
**Status:** FIXED. Follow-up sweep after the `uw-gex-fallback` fix (below): grepped every `console.warn`/`console.error` in `providers/`, `nighthawk/`, `zerodte/` for the same "expected condition logged at misleading severity" shape.

**Found a real second instance:** `polygon-options-gex.ts:220` ‚Äî `[polygon-gex] 0 I:SPX contracts for ${expiry} @ ${spot}... Verify POLYGON_API_KEY is a valid key...`. `expiry` defaults to `todayEtYmd()`, so on any non-trading day (today's holiday included) there is genuinely NO listed 0DTE expiry ‚Äî 0 contracts is expected, and the "verify your API key" hint is actively misleading, not just noisy. Confirmed this is live, reachable code (not dead post the `spx-desk.ts` single-source migration mentioned in a nearby comment) ‚Äî traced its one remaining call site through `fetchPolygonOdteGexRows` to `largo/run-tool.ts`, so a member's Largo question can trigger this exact path.

**Fix:** reused the same `isLiveOdteSession()` just built for the UW fix (no duplicate logic) ‚Äî warn with the API-key hint only during a real trading session; log at `info` off-hours/holiday. `unusual-whales.ts` and `polygon-options-gex.ts` have no existing import relationship in either direction ‚Äî checked before adding one ‚Äî so this doesn't introduce a circular dependency.

**Checked and correctly NOT touched:** several `console.warn` calls in `nighthawk/edition-builder.ts` ("stage_X zeroed ‚Äî recap-only fallback") looked superficially similar (a fallback path warning) but are a different class ‚Äî a recap-only Night Hawk edition is worth knowing about on ANY day, not just an expected off-hours artifact like a 0-contract count. Applying the same off-hours suppression there would hide genuinely worth-surfacing degradations, not just noise. Investigated properly before deciding not to touch, not skipped by assumption.

**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit`, 780/780 tests (no new tests needed ‚Äî this call site reuses the already-tested `isLiveOdteSession()`, no new pure logic introduced), `npm run build` clean.

## üü° FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî `[uw-gex-fallback] ... 0 usable strikes` logged as Railway "error" for an expected off-hours/holiday condition
**Status:** FIXED. User-reported (live Railway log screenshot) the same message already investigated and confirmed non-actionable earlier tonight (market holiday, no fresh 0DTE contracts, fallback chain succeeds via tier 2) ‚Äî but seeing it tagged `level: "error"` in Railway's UI again meant the underlying noise problem itself was still worth fixing, even though the condition it reports is benign.

**Root cause:** `console.warn()` writes to stderr in Node.js, and Railway's log pipeline classifies anything on stderr as `"error"` severity ‚Äî it doesn't distinguish `warn` from `error` at the platform level. This exact class of bug already has a fixed precedent one tier earlier in the same function (`finding #76`: the SUCCESS path was downgraded from warn to info because a healthy per-cycle build was reading as a red Railway error). The FAILURE-then-fallback path (tier 1 returns 0 rows, tier 2 picks it up) had the same problem, just never fixed.

**Fix:** `fetchUwOdteGexLadder()` (`unusual-whales.ts`) now only warns on "0 usable strikes" when it happens during a real trading session (`isLiveOdteSession()`, new exported pure function: `isTradingDayEt` + `isSpxEngineCronWindow`, both already-established helpers) ‚Äî off-hours/weekend/holiday occurrences log at `info` instead. Deliberately NOT a blanket downgrade to info: if UW's response shape changes or a parsing bug starts filtering every row, "0 usable strikes" during a genuine trading session is still a real signal worth surfacing at warn ‚Äî only the known-benign off-hours case is quieted. The `catch` block for actual thrown errors (network failures, 503s) is untouched ‚Äî those are genuine degradations regardless of time of day.

**Note on process, not just the fix:** caught and corrected my own mistake while shipping this ‚Äî ran `git reset --hard origin/main` to start a fresh branch without checking `git status` first, which discarded this exact uncommitted fix. Recovered immediately from recent context (had just written and tested it) and reapplied it exactly; the lesson (always check status before a hard reset, no exceptions for "just switching branches") is now something to actually hold to, not just state as policy.

**Verification:** new `unusual-whales.test.ts` ‚Äî 4 tests covering holiday, weekend, off-hours-on-a-trading-day, and during-the-window cases for the extracted `isLiveOdteSession()`. 780/780 total tests, `tsc --noEmit` + build clean.

## üßÝ Database query failures now captured at the source ‚Äî every dbQuery() call site, not N audits
**Status:** SHIPPED. Follow-through on the item flagged earlier tonight as "needs a proper audit before implementing" ‚Äî did the audit, it came back clean, shipped the fix.

**The audit:** grepped every direct `dbQuery(` call site (20 files total ‚Äî far fewer than assumed) and checked each for existing `captureError` usage. **Zero of the 19 non-`error-sink.ts` call sites already capture query failures.** No double-counting risk, so the better fix (capture once inside the shared function, not audit/patch N call sites) is safe to ship.

**Fix:** `dbQuery()` (`db.ts`) now fire-and-forgets a `captureError(err, {source:"db_query", scope: <truncated query text>})` on any final (non-retryable, or retries-exhausted) failure ‚Äî never awaited, so a fully-down DB can't compound latency onto the already-failing caller. Added `"db_query"` to `ErrorSource`.

**The real bug caught before shipping, not after:** `captureError` ‚Üí `persistErrorEvent` ‚Üí `dbQuery(INSERT INTO error_events...)` runs back through this exact function. If the DB is genuinely fully down (not just the original query), that INSERT fails too ‚Äî which would call the same capture path again, unboundedly. Added a module-level re-entrancy guard (`capturingQueryFailure`): a query failure while a capture attempt is already in flight just logs to console instead of re-entering `captureError`. Traced the full recursion scenario by hand before shipping rather than trusting it "probably" wouldn't happen. Side effect, judged acceptable: during a genuine full outage, concurrent unrelated query failures also get suppressed while one capture attempt is in flight ‚Äî a natural throttle against amplifying load on an already-struggling DB, not just an artifact of the guard; nothing is silently lost since the console.warn fallback still hits Railway's own logs.

**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit`, 776/776 tests, `npm run build` clean. No new unit test ‚Äî same established boundary as every other piece of `dbQuery`/connection-retry internals in this file (untested by design, verified live); will confirm via `error_events` rows tagged `source='db_query'` after deploy if any real failures occur.

## ‚úÖ Post-deploy live verification 2026-07-03 07:44 UTC ‚Äî PR #308/#309/#311/#312 all confirmed live; the new wiring immediately surfaced a real finding
**Status:** VERIFIED + one new OPEN item found (below), not by luck ‚Äî this is the BIE discovery wiring (PR #312) working exactly as designed on its first live run.

- Railway deploy `dababb04` (commit `b9e2ed64`, PR #312) reached **SUCCESS** ‚Äî confirmed via the Railway API (deployments query), not assumed. This commit's lineage includes #308, #309, and #311, so **all four are now confirmed live together** ‚Äî the earlier #309-unconfirmed gap is closed.
- `/api/ready` ‚Üí `{"ok":true,"db":"connected"}`.
- NVDA/SPY/QQQ/AAPL GEX heatmap checks returned empty chains right now (`"No options-chain data for this ticker"`) ‚Äî expected: market holiday, off-hours, no warm cron running, not a regression (the #308 total-reconciliation fix was already confirmed with real live data at 06:26 UTC earlier today).
- **The new BIE discovery wiring (PR #312) is live and working**: hit `/api/admin/bie-report` with a real admin session and it immediately surfaced `Data-correctness FLAG [cross-provider/mark]: 6/6 held contracts NOT found in snapshot or chain (e.g. ASTS 2026-07-17 120C, ASTS 2026-10-16 75C, BABA 2026-07-17 80P, HIMS 2026-07-17 38C, NOK 2028-12-15 15C)` ‚Äî a real, already-decided finding from the `data-correctness` cron that BIE had no visibility into before this session. This is exactly the "impactful, not just plumbing" bar from `docs/bie/DESIGN-NOTES.md`.

**Investigated the new finding, not just logged it (per report-first policy ‚Äî do not fix on one unconfirmed data point):**
- Confirmed via direct Polygon calls that the flagged NOK 2028-12-15 15C contract genuinely exists (`/v3/reference/options/contracts`, status OK) **and** has real market data on its own per-contract snapshot (`/v3/snapshot/options/NOK/O:NOK281215C00015000` ‚Äî live greeks, IV, last trade) ‚Äî so the underlying data is NOT missing from Polygon; the gap is in how the app looks it up.
- Traced the real (non-audit) code path: `fetchNwOptionChain()` (`polygon-options-gex.ts:55`) calls `resolveSpotSnapshot(underlying)` for the STOCK first; if that returns `spot === 0`, the function returns `null` **before** it ever tries the strike-hint-widened band fetch ‚Äî so a held position's exact strike being in the widened band doesn't matter if the underlying's own snapshot has no fresh spot price. The correctness verifier (`nights-watch-verifier.ts`) calls this exact same shared path (`getNwChain` ‚Üí `fetchNwOptionChain`, with `strikeHints` passed through identically), so this is not a checker-only artifact ‚Äî the real member-facing valuation (`nights-watch/enrichment.ts`) shares the same chain cache and would hit the same wall.
- **Superseded by a better-evidenced root cause, found independently by Cursor (the parallel agent) while this entry was being written: PR #314.** My "market holiday, spot=0" hypothesis above was a reasonable read of the code but wrong ‚Äî Cursor's PR proves via direct prod probes (`GET /api/cron/nights-watch-warm?force=1` ‚Üí `snapshot_contracts: 0` while `distinct_chains: 6`) that the real cause is `nights-watch-warm`'s snapshot pass being **shard-filtered** ‚Äî only tickers matching the current minute-shard got warmed, leaving 5/6 held legs cold on every tick, independent of market hours or holidays. `nights-watch-verifier` then only read the (cold) warmed cache, false-flagging real, live-priced contracts as "unlisted." Fix: never shard-filter the ‚â§250-OCC snapshot warm pass (sharding still applies to the heavier chain/GEX fallback only), plus a bounded upstream audit-probe fallback in the verifier itself for when caches are legitimately cold (off-hours, post-deploy). Also fixes a real latent bug found along the way: `ymdOf()` used local-timezone `Date` getters instead of UTC, which could shift OCC/expiry keys on a non-UTC replica.
- **Verification:** PR #314 all-green (CI + auto-merge enabled), 2 new test files. Confirms the value of investigating rather than guessing ‚Äî my hypothesis was plausible but the direct prod evidence Cursor pulled (shard math, not calendar) was the real answer. Re-check not needed Monday specifically anymore; #314 fixes the actual mechanism regardless of trading day.

## üßÝ BIE Stage 4 ‚Äî `alert_audit_log` schema shipped (step 2 of the rollout in `AUDIT-TRAIL-SCHEMA.md`)

`zerodte_setup_log` and `nighthawk_play_outcomes`/`nighthawk_editions` remain the system of record for their own UI/grading logic ‚Äî nothing about them changes. No code reads or writes `alert_audit_log` yet; that's the next two PRs in the rollout (0DTE write-path, then Night Hawk write-path), deliberately kept separate since they touch live scan/dossier logic and deserve their own review, not bundled into a schema change that by itself cannot regress anything.

## üßÝ BIE ‚Äî discovery now reads the already-running data-integrity/data-correctness validators
**Status:** SHIPPED. First concrete step against the user's formal primary-objective charter (`docs/bie/FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`): data integrity outranks trade-recommendation quality, and BIE must never invent a correctness verdict ‚Äî only surface what a real validation layer already found.

**What was already true, that BIE was blind to:** `data-correctness` (every 30min RTH) and `data-integrity` (every 5min RTH) crons already run a full layered validation sweep (shadow-recompute/invariant/sanity/cross-provider/cross-tool/freshness) across heat maps, SPX desk, HELIX flows, Night's Watch, Night Hawk, track record ‚Äî and `data-integrity` already auto-opens real incidents (`admin_incidents`) on any discrepancy. Neither system's output reached BIE's discovery report; discovery only knew generic cron pass/fail, not the substance of what these validators found.

**Fix:** `runBieDiscovery()` now reads `listOpenAdminIncidents()` (already existed) and the latest logged `data-correctness` run's payload (`cron_job_runs.meta_json` ‚Äî reads the already-decided result, never re-runs the sweep). `formatDiscovery()` surfaces every open incident as a finding unconditionally (these are pre-confirmed by the validator, not a BIE guess), every data-correctness FLAG as a finding (a probable wrong displayed number), and flags a coverage-gap warning when a market-hours run had zero independently-confirmed metrics (consistency-only ‚âÝ a guarantee ‚Äî the same honesty the underlying scorecard already enforces, now propagated to BIE's report instead of silently dropped).

**Verification:** 5 new regression tests (`bie.test.ts`) covering: incidents always become findings with no threshold, no incidents means no section, correctness FLAGs surface as findings, the zero-independently-confirmed coverage-gap case, and a genuinely healthy run producing a summary line with no findings. 773/773 total pass, `tsc --noEmit` + build clean.

## üî¥ P0 SECURITY ‚Äî Postgres credential printed into Railway build logs since 2026-06-30; ACTION NEEDED: rotate the password
**Status:** OPEN ‚Äî code fix shipped this PR (`fix/railway-build-command-secret-leak`), **but the exposed credential itself still needs to be rotated by the user; that is not something this PR can do.**

**Found while diagnosing a #308/#309 deploy-healthcheck incident, using Railway API access granted this session (project-scoped token).** Pulling the failed deployment's build log to find its root cause surfaced `railway.toml`'s build command:

```
buildCommand = "DATABASE_URL=$DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL npm run build"
```

Buildkit echoes the literal RUN command it executes into the build log, with inline shell-variable assignments already expanded ‚Äî so every build since this line was added (`railway.toml`'s introduction, commit `1c0bca7`, 2026-06-30) printed the **real Postgres connection string, including its plaintext password,** into that build's log output. Confirmed directly: the build log for the failed deployment contains the fully-expanded `DATABASE_URL=postgres://postgres:<password>@...` string, twice. Docker/Buildkit's own linter has been flagging this exact class of problem on every build (`SecretsUsedInArgOrEnv` warnings) ‚Äî the same pattern affects essentially every other secret passed as an `ARG`/`ENV` at build time (`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `CLERK_SECRET_KEY`, `CRON_SECRET`, `POLYGON_API_KEY`, `RAILWAY_TOKEN`, `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`, `UW_API_KEY`, `VOYAGE_API_KEY`, `WHOP_API_KEY`, and others) ‚Äî those are set as Docker build args/env (not printed in a RUN command's literal text the way `DATABASE_URL` was here), so they don't have the same *log-echo* exposure, but the linter warning on all of them is worth a follow-up read.

**Blast radius:** every Railway build log since 2026-06-30 (multiple days, many builds/deploys) contains the plaintext DB password. Anyone with read access to this project's Railway build-log history ‚Äî not just deploy/dashboard access ‚Äî has been able to read it.

**Fix (this PR):** `scripts/railway-build.sh` ‚Äî a wrapper script that does the `DATABASE_URL=$DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL` assignment via `export` *inside* the script rather than inline in the command string Buildkit echoes. `railway.toml`'s `buildCommand` now reads `bash scripts/railway-build.sh` ‚Äî the printed build step is just that literal text, never the secret value. `DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL` (not `DATABASE_URL`) is still required at build time for the same reason as before: the build phase can't reach Railway's private network (`postgres.railway.internal`), only the public host.

**Action needed (user, cannot be done from a PR):**
1. **Rotate the Postgres password** (Railway dashboard ‚Üí Postgres plugin ‚Üí regenerate credentials) ‚Äî the exposed one must be treated as compromised regardless of how unlikely actual unauthorized access is, since the exposure window is multi-day.
2. After rotating, this service's `DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_PUBLIC_URL` env vars update automatically (Railway re-injects the new value) ‚Äî a fresh deploy after rotation will pick it up cleanly with this PR's fix already in place, so it won't get re-leaked.
3. Worth a follow-up: audit the other `SecretsUsedInArgOrEnv`-flagged vars (build-time `ARG`/`ENV`, not the log-echo pattern above) for the same class of risk ‚Äî out of scope for this PR, which only fixes the confirmed active leak.

## üüÝ OPEN 2026-07-03 06:26 UTC ‚Äî Railway deploy healthcheck failure after #308/#309 merges; BIE has zero visibility into this failure class
**Status:** OPEN ‚Äî pending user redeploy action; root cause not yet confirmed (most likely transient, see below).

**What happened (user-reported, live Railway mobile screenshots):** a deploy immediately following the #308/#309 merges showed `5/5 replicas never became healthy!` / `Healthcheck failed!` in Railway, after 7 retry attempts against `/api/ready` all failing with "service unavailable" over a 2-minute window. Railway correctly kept serving the last-healthy deployment rather than cutting traffic over (no downtime observed).

**Confirmed live right now (direct production test, not the audit script ‚Äî see prior entry's caveat below):** `curl .../api/market/gex-heatmap?ticker=NVDA` with a valid bearer token shows `total === Œ£(strike_totals)` exactly across all 4 lenses (gex/vex/dex/charm) ‚Äî **PR #308's fix IS live and correct.** PR #309's fix (Polygon AAPL pagination) could not be directly confirmed the same way (no public endpoint exercises `fetchPolygonOiByExpiry` without a full authenticated Largo/Night Hawk session) ‚Äî **its live status is unconfirmed.** Correcting the previous entry below: the "46 pass / 0 issues" full-site sweep ran against whatever was the last-*healthy* deployment at that moment, which is NOT proof both #308 and #309 were live ‚Äî only the direct GEX total check is.

**Why this is unlikely to be a #308/#309 code bug:** `/api/ready` (`src/app/api/ready/route.ts`) checks DB connectivity only (`pingDatabaseConnectivity()` ‚Üí a bare `SELECT 1`) ‚Äî explicitly NOT gated on `ensureSchema()`/migrations ("no migration lock" per its own comment). Neither #308's diff (`round-floats.ts`, `gex-heatmap/route.ts`) nor #309's diff (`polygon-options-gex.ts`) touches DB connectivity, startup, or imports anything new. All 5 replicas failing identically with connection-level "service unavailable" (not an app-level 503 JSON body) points at a platform/DB-layer hiccup during that specific rolling restart, not application logic ‚Äî plausibly a transient PgBouncer/Postgres connection-pressure spike from 5 replicas cold-booting close together (the exact class of issue `provider-health-reconcile`'s retry logic and #307's advisory-lock fix already target, though #307's own deploy had already gone out and succeeded earlier).

**Why BIE did not catch this (direct answer to the question asked):** it structurally *cannot*, yet. BIE's error capture (`error_events` via `captureError()`) is written **by the running application** ‚Äî a replica that never passes `/api/ready` never serves real traffic and never gets the chance to emit an application-level error; the failure lives entirely in Railway's build/deploy/healthcheck layer, which BIE has **zero access to today**. This is precisely the Stage 3 gap already logged in `docs/bie/FULL-SYSTEM-AWARENESS.md`: *"Railway deployment status/errors ‚Äî Blocker: No Railway API token configured."* `cron_job_runs`/discovery cron-health checks don't cover this either ‚Äî a failed deploy isn't a cron job. No amount of the already-shipped Stage 2 work (frontend/backend error capture, cron health, Redis/Postgres pool stats) closes this gap; only Railway API access does. `RAILWAY_TOKEN` was added to Railway's service env vars (visible to the deployed app) but is still not visible in this Claude Code sandbox's own shell as of this check ‚Äî needs the user to confirm it's set as a **sandbox/session** env var, not (only) a Railway service var; these are two different stores (see task #20).

**Action needed (user):** tap **Redeploy** on the current `main` (commit `c601fd9`, which is a strict superset containing both #308 and #309) from the Railway app to get a clean, non-overlapping rolling deploy attempt ‚Äî the two back-to-back merges likely caused two overlapping rolling deploys competing for DB connections during boot, which a single clean redeploy avoids.

**Verification pending:** once redeployed, re-run the NVDA GEX total check (still expected to pass, already confirmed) and get a live confirmation of the Polygon AAPL pagination fix specifically.

## üü° FIXED 2026-07-03 ‚Äî AAPL options chain truncated: static 12-page guard understating walls/OI/IV
**Status:** FIXED (`fix/polygon-oi-by-expiry-pagination`). User-reported (live Railway log screenshots) recurring `[polygon-gex] fetchPolygonOiByExpiry(AAPL) truncated: hit 12-page guard with next_url still set ‚Äî chain incomplete, walls/OI/IV understated`, firing repeatedly over several minutes.

**Root cause:** `fetchPolygonOiByExpiry` (`polygon-options-gex.ts`) capped pagination at a flat 12 pages (3,000 contracts) regardless of how many contracts AAPL's live chain actually has. This is the exact same anti-pattern the codebase already diagnosed and fixed once before for `fetchHeatmapBand` (see the `HEATMAP_PAGE_GUARD` comment: "previously raised 16‚Üí40 for SPX, truncated again the same day... chasing the live chain size with another static number is the same bug recurring on a slower clock" ‚Äî SPX needed 46 pages / 11,254 contracts). This function had its own unprotected copy of the same bug.

**Fix ‚Äî not just "raise the number":** this function is called from a LIVE per-request path (`largo/run-tool.ts`'s Largo tool, and `nighthawk/option-chain-prompt.ts`), unlike the heatmap's cron-warmed build ‚Äî so an unbounded/very-generous page count would add real latency to a member waiting on a Largo answer. Instead, the loop now stops on the function's actual completion condition: Polygon returns contracts sorted by `expiration_date` ascending, so once `limit + 1` distinct expiries have been seen, every one of the target `limit` nearest expiries is provably fully closed out (a later expiry has started, so no more contracts for an earlier one can arrive) ‚Äî stop there instead of guessing a page count. A 40-page backstop (matching the old proven-sufficient heatmap floor) still bounds worst-case latency. Both call sites use small `limit`s (6 and 12), so 40 pages is comfortable headroom.

**Verification:** 763/763 tests, `tsc --noEmit` + build clean. No unit test added ‚Äî this function does live Polygon network I/O with no DI seam (same established boundary as this file's one existing test, which only covers the pure `resolveHeatmapPageGuard`).

## üü¢ FIXED ‚Äî `provider-health-reconcile` cron intermittent PgBouncer `server_login_retry` failures (ops #242)
**Status:** FIXED (`cursor/provider-health-reconcile-0fcb`).

**Where:** `dbQuery()` in `src/lib/db.ts` ‚Äî no retry on transient PgBouncer login blips. `provider-health-reconcile` (and other crons) logged `failed` rows when PgBouncer briefly returned `server login has been failing, cached error: connect failed (server_login_retry)`. `hit-cron.mjs` HTTP retries amplified this into 3‚Äì4 failed `cron_job_runs` rows per scheduled tick before one `ok`.

**Evidence:** Postgres `cron_job_runs` 2026-07-02 ‚Äî 9/90 provider-health-reconcile runs in 24h failed, all with the same PgBouncer message; latest run `ok` at 13:10:35Z after transient blip at 13:10:16‚Äì25Z. Ops collect fingerprint `7dcb62ad3be6` cleared once latest run recovered.

**Fix:** `isTransientPgError()` in `src/lib/db-transient.ts`; `dbQuery()` retries up to 3√ó with pool reset + backoff on transient errors (configurable via `PG_QUERY_RETRIES` / `PG_QUERY_RETRY_DELAY_MS`).

**Verification:** 5 unit tests in `db-transient.test.ts`; `npx tsc --noEmit` clean.
